PREFACE
   This county code of Minidoka County, as supplemented, contains ordinances up
to and including ordinance 2024-12-2, passed December 2, 2024. Ordinances of
the county adopted after said ordinance supersede the provisions of this code
to the extent that they are in conflict or inconsistent therewith. Consult the
county office in order to ascertain whether any particular provision of the
code has been amended, superseded or repealed.
American Legal Publishing
Cincinnati, Ohio
ORDINANCES PENDING CODIFICATION
Listed ordinances have been passed, but they have not been incorporated into
the code and they may not show the original ordinances in their entirety.
Please contact the office of the clerk if there are any questions concerning
the ordinances listed.
ADOPTING ORDINANCE
ORDINANCE NO. 2016-10-17
AN ORDINANCE ADOPTING THE COMPILED ORDINANCES ENACTED BY THE MINIDOKA COUNTY
BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS AS THE MINIDOKA COUNTY CODE, PROVIDING FOR PERPETUAL
CODIFICATION IN THE FUTURE, PROHIBITING UNAUTHORIZED MODIFICATION OF THE COUNTY
CODE, SUPERSEDING PRIOR MINIDOKA COUNTY ORDINANCES OF A GENERAL NATURE THE
SUBSTANCE OF WHICH IS INCORPORATED HEREIN, AND PROVIDING THAT THE MINIDOKA
COUNTY CODE SHALL BE EFFECTIVE UPON THE DATE OF PUBLICATION OF A SUMMARY OF
THIS ORDINANCE IN THE OFFICIAL NEWSPAPER OF MINIDOKA COUNTY.
BE IT ORDAINED by the board of commissioners of Minidoka County, Idaho as
follows:
   Section 1: From and after the date of passage of this ordinance, the county
code of Minidoka County, Idaho, prepared by Sterling Codifiers, containing the
compilation of all ordinances of a general nature together with the changes
made to said ordinances, under the direction of the governing body of the
county, shall be accepted in all courts as provided by law as the official code
and law of Minidoka County as enacted by the county commissioners.
   Section 2: There is hereby adopted, as a method of perpetual codification,
the loose-leaf type of binding together with the continuous supplement service,
provided by Sterling Codifiers, whereby each newly adopted ordinance of a
general and permanent nature amending, altering, adding or deleting provisions
of the official county code is identified by the proper catchline and is
inserted in the proper place in each of the official copies, one copy of which
shall be maintained in the office of the county clerk, certified as to
correctness and available for inspection at any and all times that said office
is regularly open.
   Section 3: All ordinances of a general nature included in this official
county code shall be considered as a continuation of said ordinance provision
and the fact that some provisions have been deliberately eliminated by the
governing body shall not serve to cause any interruption in the continuous
effectiveness of ordinances included in said official county code. All
ordinances of a special nature, such as tax levy ordinances, bond ordinances,
franchises, ordinances addressing particular described or mapped lands or
vacating ordinances shall continue in full force and effect unless specifically
repealed or amended by a provision of the county code. Such ordinances of
special nature are not intended to be included in the official county code.
   Section 4: It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to
change or amend by additions or deletions, any part or portion of such code, or
to insert or delete pages or portions thereof, or to alter or tamper with such
code in any manner whatsoever which will cause the law of the county to be
misrepresented thereby.
   Section 5: All ordinances or parts of ordinances in conflict herewith, are,
to the extent of such conflict, hereby repealed.
   Section 6: This ordinance shall be recorded and the code adopted hereby
shall be retained by the Minidoka County clerk and shall be in full force and
effect from and after its passage, approval and publication in book form as
provided by law.
PASSED by the board of county commissioners on the 17 day of October, 2016 by a
roll call vote reflected in the minutes.
          
   Chair of the Board
ATTEST:
          
   Minidoka County Clerk
TITLE 1
ADMINISTRATION
CHAPTER 1
MINIDOKA COUNTY CODE
SECTION:
1-1-1: Title
1-1-2: Acceptance
1-1-3: Amendments
1-1-4: Code Alterations
1-1-1: TITLE:
Upon adoption by the board of county commissioners, this code is hereby
declared to be and shall hereafter constitute the official county code of
Minidoka County. This code of ordinances shall be known and cited as the
MINIDOKA COUNTY CODE and is hereby published by authority of the county
commissioners and shall be supplemented to incorporate the most recent
legislation of the county as provided in section
1-1-3 of this chapter. Any reference to the number of any section contained
herein shall be understood to refer to the position of the same number, its
appropriate chapter and title heading, and to the general penalty clause
relating thereto, as well as to the section itself, when reference is made to
this code by title in any legal documents. (2016 Code)
1-1-2: ACCEPTANCE:
This code, as hereby presented in printed form, shall hereafter be received
without further proof in all courts and in administrative tribunals of this
state as the ordinances of the county of general and permanent effect, except
the excluded ordinances enumerated in section
1-2-1 of this title. (2016 Code)
1-1-3: AMENDMENTS:
Any ordinance amending this code shall set forth the title, chapter and section
number of the section or sections to be amended, and this shall constitute
sufficient compliance with any statutory requirement pertaining to the
amendment or revision by ordinance of any part of this code. All such
amendments or revisions by ordinance shall be immediately forwarded to the
codifiers, and the said ordinance material shall be prepared for insertion in
its proper place in each copy of this code. Each such replacement page shall be
properly identified and shall be inserted in each individual copy of this code.
(2016 Code)
1-1-4: CODE ALTERATIONS:
It shall be deemed unlawful for any person to alter, change, replace or deface
in any way any section or any page of this code in such a manner that the
meaning of any phrase or order may be changed or omitted. Said code, while in
actual possession of officials and other interested persons, shall be and
remain the property of the county and shall be returned to the office of the
county clerk when directed so to do by order of the county commissioners. (2016
Code)
CHAPTER 2
SAVING CLAUSE
SECTION:
1-2-1: Repeal Of General Ordinances
1-2-2: Court Proceedings
1-2-3: Severability Clause
1-2-1: REPEAL OF GENERAL ORDINANCES:
   A.   Ordinances Repealed And Ordinances Saved From Repeal: All general
ordinances of the county passed prior to the adoption of this code are hereby
repealed, except such as are included in this code or are by necessary
implication herein reserved from repeal (subject to the saving clauses
contained in the following sections), and excluding the following ordinances
which are not hereby repealed:
      1.   Tax levy ordinances.
      2.   Appropriation ordinances.
      3.   Ordinances relating to boundaries and annexations.
      4.   Franchise ordinances and other ordinances granting special rights to
persons or corporations.
      5.   Contract ordinances and ordinances authorizing the execution of a
contract or the issuance of warrants.
      6.   Salary ordinances.
      7.   Ordinances establishing, naming or vacating streets, public ways or
other public places in the county.
      8.   Local improvement districts.
      9.   Bond ordinances.
      10.   Ordinances relating to elections.
      11.   Ordinances relating to the transfer or acceptance of real estate by
or from the county.
      12.   All special ordinances.
   B.   Limitations On Repeal: The repeal of the ordinances, as provided in
subsection A of this section, shall not affect any debt or fee which is
accrued, any duty imposed, any penalty incurred, nor any action or proceeding
commenced under or by virtue of the ordinances repealed or the term of office
of any person holding office at the time these ordinances take effect; nor
shall the repeal of any ordinance have the effect of reviving any ordinance
heretofore repealed or superseded. (2016 Code)
1-2-2: COURT PROCEEDINGS:
   A.   Prior Acts: No new ordinance shall be construed or held to repeal a
former ordinance whether such former ordinance is expressly repealed or not, as
to any offense committed against such former ordinance or as to any act done,
any penalty, forfeiture or punishment so incurred, or any right accrued or
claim arising under the former ordinance, or in any way whatever to affect any
such offense or act so committed or so done, or any penalty, forfeiture or
punishment so incurred or any right accrued or claim arising before the new
ordinance takes effect, save only that the proceedings thereafter shall conform
to the ordinance in force at the time of such proceeding, so far as
practicable. If any penalty, forfeiture or punishment may be mitigated by any
provision of a new ordinance, such provision may be, by consent of the party
affected, applied to any judgment announced after the new ordinance takes
effect.
   B.   Extend To All Repeals: This section shall extend to all repeals, either
by express words or implication, whether the repeal is in the ordinance making
any new provisions upon the same subject or in any other ordinance.
   C.   Current And Pending Actions: Nothing contained in this chapter shall be
construed as abating any action now pending under or by virtue of any general
ordinance of the county herein repealed, and the provisions of all general
ordinances contained in this code shall be deemed to be continuing provisions
and not a new enactment of the same provisions; nor shall this chapter be
deemed as discontinuing, abating, modifying or altering any penalty accrued or
to accrue, or as affecting the liability of any person, firm or corporation, or
as waiving any right of the county under any ordinance or provision thereof in
force at the time of the adoption of this code. (2016 Code)
1-2-3: SEVERABILITY CLAUSE:
If any section, subsection, paragraph, sentence, clause or phrase of this code,
or any part hereof, or any portion adopted by reference or any codes or
portions of codes adopted herein is for any reason held to be unconstitutional
or invalid or ineffective by any court of competent jurisdiction, such decision
shall not affect the validity or effectiveness of the remaining portions of
this code, or any part hereof, or any portion adopted by reference or any codes
or portions of codes adopted herein. The board of county commissioners hereby
declares that it would have passed each section, subsection, paragraph,
sentence, clause or phrase thereof irrespective of the fact that any one or
more sections, subsections, paragraphs, sentences, clauses or phrases be
declared unconstitutional, invalid or ineffective. (2016 Code)
CHAPTER 3
DEFINITIONS AND INTERPRETATIONS
SECTION:
1-3-1: General Rules Of Interpretation
1-3-2: Definitions, General
1-3-3: Catchlines
1-3-1: GENERAL RULES OF INTERPRETATION:
   A.   Liberal Construction: All general provisions, terms, phrases and
expressions contained in this code shall be liberally construed in order that
the true intent and meaning of the board of county commissioners may be fully
carried out.
   B.   Minimum Requirements: In the interpretation and application of any
provision of this code, it shall be held to be the minimum requirements adopted
for the promotion of the public health, safety and general welfare.
   C.   Computation Of Time: Whenever a notice is required to be given or an
act to be done in a certain length of time before any proceeding shall be had,
the day on which such notice is given or such act is done shall not be counted
in computing the time, but the day on which such proceeding is to be held shall
be counted.
   D.   Delegation Of Authority: Whenever a provision appears requiring the
head of a department or some other county officer to do some act or perform
some duty, it shall be construed to authorize the head of the department or
other officer to designate, delegate and authorize subordinates to perform the
required act or perform the duty unless the terms of the provision or section
specify otherwise.
   E.   Gender: The use of any gender based pronoun should not be construed to
be gender biased, but is only used for grammatical simplicity.
   F.   Joint Authority: All words giving a joint authority to three (3) or
more persons or officers shall be construed as giving such authority to a
majority of such persons or officers.
   G.   May/Shall: The word "may" is permissive; the word "shall" is mandatory.
   H.   Nontechnical And Technical Words: Words and phrases shall be construed
according to the common and approved usage of the language, but technical words
and phrases and such others as may have acquired a peculiar and appropriate
meaning in law shall be construed and understood according to such meaning.
   I.   Number: A word importing the singular number only may extend and be
applied to several persons and things as well as to one person and thing.
   J.   Officers And Employees Generally: Whenever any officer or employee is
referred to by title only, such reference shall be construed as if followed by
the words "of Minidoka County".
   K.   Tense: Words used in the past or present tense include the future as
well as the past and present.
   L.   Ordinance: The word "ordinance" contained in the ordinances of the
county has been changed in the content of this code to "title", "chapter",
"section" and/or "subsection" or words of like import for organizational and
clarification purposes only. Such change to the county's ordinances is not
meant to amend passage and effective dates of such original ordinances. (2016
Code)
1-3-2: DEFINITIONS, GENERAL:
The following words and phrases, whenever used in the ordinances of the county,
and this code, shall be construed as defined in this section unless from the
context a different meaning is intended or unless a different meaning is
specifically defined and more particularly directed to the use of such words or
phrases:
   COUNTY: The county of Minidoka, state of Idaho.
   COUNTY COMMISSIONERS OR BOARD: The board of county commissioners of Minidoka
County, Idaho.
   IC: Idaho Code.
   LAW: Denotes applicable federal law, the constitution and statutes of the
state of Idaho, the ordinances of the county of Minidoka, and, when
appropriate, any and all rules and regulations which may be promulgated
thereunder.
   PERSON: Includes a natural person, joint venture, joint stock company,
partnership, association, club, company, corporation, business, trust,
organization, or the manager, lessee, agent, servant, officer or employee of
any of them.
   STATE: The state of Idaho. (2016 Code)
1-3-3: CATCHLINES:
The catchlines of the several sections of this code are intended as mere
catchwords to indicate the content of the section and shall not be deemed or
taken to be titles of such sections, nor be deemed to govern, limit, modify or
in any manner affect the scope, meaning or intent of the provisions of any
section of this code, nor, unless expressly so provided, shall they be so
deemed when any of such sections, including the catchlines, are amended or
reenacted. (2016 Code)
CHAPTER 4
GENERAL PENALTY
SECTION:
1-4-1: General Penalty
1-4-2: Application Of Provisions
1-4-3: Liability Of Officers
1-4-1: GENERAL PENALTY:
Any person convicted of a violation of any section or provision of this code,
where no other penalty is set forth, shall be punished by a fine not to exceed
one thousand dollars ($1,000.00) or by imprisonment not to exceed six (6)
months, or by both such fine and imprisonment, for each offense; or by a fine
not to exceed three hundred dollars ($300.00) with no imprisonment, when the
offense is designated as an infraction by state law or by any section or
provision of this code. (2016 Code)
1-4-2: APPLICATION OF PROVISIONS:
   A.   Application Of Penalty:
      1.   The penalty provided in this chapter shall be applicable to every
section of this code the same as though it were a part of each and every
separate section. Any person convicted of a violation of any section of this
code where any duty is prescribed or obligation imposed or where any action
which is of a continuing nature is forbidden or is declared to be unlawful
shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor unless otherwise provided. A separate
offense shall be deemed committed upon each day such duty or obligation remains
unperformed or such act continues unless otherwise specifically provided in
this code.
      2.   Whenever the doing of any act or the omission to do any act
constitutes a breach of any section or provision of this code, and there shall
be no fine or penalty specifically declared for such breach, the provisions of
this chapter shall apply.
   B.   Imposition Of Penalty: In all cases where the same offense is made
punishable or is created by different clauses or sections of this code, the
prosecuting officer may elect under which to proceed; but not more than one
recovery shall be had against the same person for the same offense; provided,
that the revocation of a license or permit shall not be considered a recovery
or penalty so as to bar any other penalty being enforced.
   C.   Breach Of Provisions: Whenever the doing of any act or the omission to
do any act constitutes a breach of any section or provision of this code and
there shall be no fine or penalty specifically declared for such breach, the
provisions of this chapter shall apply. (2016 Code)
1-4-3: LIABILITY OF OFFICERS:
No provision of this code designating the duties of any officer or employee
shall be so construed as to make such officer or employee liable for any fine
or penalty provided for a failure to perform such duty unless the intention of
the board of county commissioners to impose such fine or penalty on such
officer or employee is specifically and clearly expressed in the section
creating the duty. (2016 Code)
CHAPTER 5
NONDISCRIMINATION POLICY
SECTION:
1-5-1: Accessibility To Programs And Activities
1-5-1: ACCESSIBILITY TO PROGRAMS AND ACTIVITIES:
   A.   It is the policy of the county that all programs and activities shall
be accessible to, and usable by, qualified persons with disabilities.
   B.   The county shall undertake an evaluation, conducted in consultation
with citizen groups involving persons with disabilities, of its programs,
policies, procedures and facilities in order to determine those areas where
discrimination may occur.
   C.   The county shall, upon completion of said evaluation, make such
revisions, modifications, or other changes so as to fully comply with the
letter and intent of section 504 of federal rehabilitation act of 1973.
   D.   The county shall, where building modifications are required, develop
and implement a transition plan for the timely elimination of structural
barriers to citizens with disabilities. (Ord. 95-4, 6-12-1995)
CHAPTER 6
INDUSTRIAL DEVELOPMENT CORPORATION
SECTION:
1-6-1: Definitions
1-6-2: Corporation Created, Name
1-6-3: Issuance Of Charter
1-6-4: Board Of Directors
1-6-5: Powers Of Corporation
1-6-6: Rights Of Indemnification
1-6-7: Net Earnings To County
1-6-1: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this chapter, the following words shall have the following meanings:
   ACT: Chapter 27, title 50, Idaho Code.
   BOARD OF DIRECTORS: The board of directors of the public corporation.
   CORPORATION: The industrial development corporation of the board of county
commissioners, Minidoka County, Idaho.
   COUNTY: The county of Minidoka, Idaho.
   FACILITIES: Land, rights in land, buildings, structures, docks, wharves,
machinery, transmission equipment, landscaping, utilities, approaches, roadways
and parking, handling and storage areas, and similar ancillary facilities.
   INDUSTRIAL DEVELOPMENT FACILITY OR INDUSTRIAL DEVELOPMENT FACILITIES:
Manufacturing, processing, production, assembly, warehousing, transportation,
pollution control, solid waste disposal, and energy facilities. (Ord. 98-4, 6-
8-1998)
1-6-2: CORPORATION CREATED, NAME:
   A.   The county hereby creates a public corporation to carry out the purpose
of chapter 27, title 50, Idaho Code (the "act"), as that law may from time to
time hereinafter be amended.
   B.   The name of the public corporation shall be "The Industrial Development
Corporation Of The County of Minidoka, Idaho" (the "corporation"). (Ord. 98-4,
6-8-1998)
1-6-3: ISSUANCE OF CHARTER:
A charter shall be issued to the corporation by the county, which shall grant
to the corporation authority to act pursuant to the act. A copy of the initial
charter to be issued is attached as exhibit A to the ordinance codified herein.
Said charter may be amended from time to time by the county and shall contain
the limitations set forth in the act. (Ord. 98-4, 6-8-1998)
1-6-4: BOARD OF DIRECTORS:
   A.   Appointment; Quorum: The board of directors of the corporation shall be
designated and appointed by the board of county commissioners. A majority of
the members of the board of directors shall constitute a quorum.
   B.   Organization; Compensation:
      1.   The affairs of the corporation shall be conducted and carried out by
the board of directors. The board shall elect from among its own members, its
president, a vice president, a treasurer and a secretary, one of whom shall be
eligible to hold two (2) offices. The board of directors shall adopt bylaws
(rules and regulations) governing the conduct of the corporation.
      2.   Members of the board of directors shall serve with such compensation
as may be provided in the bylaws to be adopted by the board of directors.
   C.   Conflict Of Interest: No director, officer, agent or employee of the
corporation shall have, directly or indirectly, any financial interest in any
property to be included in, or any contract for, property, service or materials
to be furnished or used in connection with the industrial development
facilities financed through the corporation. (Ord. 98-4, 6-8-1998)
1-6-5: POWERS OF CORPORATION:
   A.   General Powers And Limitations: The corporation shall have all the
powers and be subject to all the limitations and provisions contained in the
act, as that law may hereinafter from time to time be amended.
   B.   Powers Enumerated: The corporation shall have all the powers granted
by, as well as limited by, the act, and shall include the following:
      1.   To construct and maintain one or more industrial development
facilities.
      2.   To lease to a lessee all or any part of any industrial development
facility for such rentals and upon such terms and conditions, including options
to purchase, as its board of directors considers advisable and not in conflict
with the act.
      3.   To sell by installment contract or otherwise and convey all or any
part of any industrial development facility for such purchase price and upon
such terms and conditions as its board of directors considers advisable, which
are not in conflict with the act.
      4.   To make loans for the purpose of providing temporary or permanent
financing or refinancing of all or part of the project cost of any industrial
development facility, including the refunding of any outstanding obligations,
mortgages, or advances issued, made, or given by any person for the project
costs; and to charge and collect interest on the loans for the loan payment
upon such terms and conditions as its board of directors considers advisable
which are not in conflict with the act.
      5.   To issue revenue bonds for the purpose of financing all or part of
the project cost of any industrial development facility and to secure the
payment of the revenue bonds as provided by the act.
      6.   As security for the payment of the principal of and interest on any
revenue bonds issued and any agreements made in connection therewith, to
mortgage, pledge, or otherwise encumber any or all of its industrial
development facilities or any part or parts thereof, whether then owned or
thereafter acquired, and to assign any lease or mortgage and repledge any
security conveyed to the corporation, and to pledge the revenues and receipts
therefrom.
      7.   To sue and be sued, complain, and defend in its corporate name.
      8.   To make contracts and to execute all instruments necessary or
convenient for the carrying out of its business.
      9.   To have a corporate seal and to use the same by causing it, or a
facsimile thereof, to be impressed or affixed or in any other manner
reproduced.
      10.   Subject to the limitations of Idaho Code section 50-2706, to borrow
money, accept grants from, or contract with, any local, state, or federal
governmental agency or with any financial public or private corporation.
      11.   To make and alter bylaws not inconsistent with its charter for the
administration and regulation of the affairs of the corporation.
      12.   To collect fees or charges from users or prospective users of
industrial development facilities to recover actual or anticipated
administrative costs.
      13.   To execute financing incidental to the powers enumerated in this
subsection.
      14.   The corporation created under this chapter may not operate any
industrial development facilities as a business other than as lessor, seller,
or lender. The other security interests and contracting for any servicing
thereof is not considered the operation of an industrial development facility.
      15.   The corporation created by this chapter may not exercise any of the
powers authorized in this section or issue any revenue bonds with respect to
any industrial development facility unless the industrial development facility
is located wholly within the boundaries of the county.
      16.   The county may not give or lend any money or property nor exercise
its power of eminent domain in aid of the corporation. This provision shall not
preclude the county from dealing with the corporation on an arms length basis.
      17.   The corporation may not issue revenue obligations, except upon
approval of the county within whose planning jurisdiction the proposed
industrial development facility lies. (Ord. 98-4, 6-8-1998)
1-6-6: RIGHTS OF INDEMNIFICATION:
Every person who was or is a party, or is threatened to be made a party to, or
is involved in, any action, suit or proceeding, whether civil, criminal,
administrative or investigative, by reason of the fact that he or a person of
whom he is the legal representative is or was a director or officer of the
corporation, or is or was serving at the request of the corporation as a
director or officer of another corporation, or as its representative in a
partnership, joint venture, trust or other enterprise, shall be indemnified and
held harmless to the fullest extent legally permissible under the law of the
state of Idaho from time to time against all expenses, liability and loss
(including attorney fees, judgments, fines and amounts paid or to be paid in
settlement), reasonably incurred or suffered by him in connection therewith.
Such rights of indemnification shall be a contract right which may be enforced
in any manner desired by such person. Such right of indemnification shall not
be exclusive of any other right which such directors, officers, or
representatives may have or hereafter acquire, and without limiting the
generality of such statement, they shall be entitled to their respective rights
of indemnification under any bylaw, agreement, vote of stockholders, provision
of law, or otherwise, as well as their rights under this section. The board of
directors may adopt bylaws from time to time with respect to indemnification to
provide at all times the fullest indemnification permitted by the laws of the
state of Idaho, and may cause the corporation to purchase and maintain
insurance on behalf of any person who is or was a director or officer of the
corporation as a director or officer of another corporation, or as its
representative in a partnership, joint venture, trust or other enterprise,
against any liability asserted against such person and incurred in any such
capacity or arising out of such status, whether or not the corporation would
have the power to indemnify such person. (Ord. 98-4, 6-8-1998)
1-6-7: NET EARNINGS TO COUNTY:
Any net earnings of the corporation, beyond those necessary for retirement of
indebtedness incurred by it, shall inure to the county and not for the benefit
of any other person. Alteration of the charter of, or dissolution of or audits
of, the corporation shall be as provided by the act and by subsequent
resolutions of the county. Upon dissolution of the corporation, title to all
property owned by the corporation shall vest in the county. (Ord. 98-4, 6-8-
1998)
CHAPTER 7
MINI-CASSIA COMMERCE AUTHORITY
SECTION:
1-7-1: Joint Powers Agreement Approval
1-7-1: JOINT POWERS AGREEMENT APPROVAL:
   A.   The board of county commissioners for Minidoka County, having reviewed
the joint powers agreement between Minidoka County, Idaho, and Cassia County,
Idaho, for formation and authorization of a joint intermodal commerce
authority, hereby approves said joint powers agreement, and the terms and
conditions thereof on behalf of Minidoka County 1 .
   B.   The chairman of the board of county commissioners and clerk are hereby
authorized to execute and attest respectively said agreement for Minidoka
County.
   C.   This section shall take effect and be in force from and after its
passage and approval and publication as by law provided, and contingent upon
Cassia County's passage of an ordinance providing for the same approvals and
terms as this section. (Ord. 05-01, 4-12-2005)
 
Notes
  1. The full and complete text of the joint powers agreement is, and shall be
1 kept, on file in the offices of the county clerks of Minidoka County and
  Cassia County.
CHAPTER 8
FINANCIAL PROVISIONS
SECTION:
1-8-1: Fees For Issuance Of Warrants Of Distraint
1-8-2: Landline And Cellular Telephone Service Fee
1-8-1: FEES FOR ISSUANCE OF WARRANTS OF DISTRAINT:
   A.   Authority: This section is adopted pursuant to the provisions of Idaho
Code section 63-1013(2), effective July 1, 2010.
   B.   Purpose: All warrants of distraint issued by the tax collector shall be
served and executed by the sheriff in the manner provided by law for the
services of executions by levy upon personal property.
   C.   Fees:
      1.   Fees allowed for issuing warrants of distraint, collection, levy and
return of the same shall be set by ordinance by the board of county
commissioners.
      2.   Minidoka County shall charge a fee of twenty dollars ($20.00) for a
warrant of distraint issued by the tax collector. (Ord. 2016-09-13-A, 9-13-
2016)
1-8-2: LANDLINE AND CELLULAR TELEPHONE SERVICE FEE:
   A.   The board of county commissioners shall assess a fee of one dollar
($1.00), beginning on October 1, 2002, to be collected by all service providers
operating within Minidoka County, for all telephone service connections, both
landline and cellular, in use within Minidoka County.
   B.   The administration of service fees shall be overseen by the Minidoka
County emergency services administrator.
   C.   All telephone service connections owned by Minidoka County shall be
exempt from the payment of the fee. (Ord. 02-03, 8-26-2002)
CHAPTER 9
GEOGRAPHIC INFORMATION SYSTEM (GIS)
SECTION:
1-9-1: Notice Of Copyright
1-9-2: Paper Maps
1-9-3: Online Services
1-9-4: GIS Data
1-9-5: GIS Data Owned By Third Parties
1-9-6: Use Of Data For Emergency Response
1-9-7: Penalties
1-9-1: NOTICE OF COPYRIGHT:
All data and maps assembled, created, maintained or published by Minidoka
County are copyrighted by the same and all rights thereto are reserved by
Minidoka County. Reproduction, conveyance, or other means of duplication
without express written permission is strictly prohibited. (Ord. 2016-02-01, 2-
1-2016)
1-9-2: PAPER MAPS:
Paper maps created using the county GIS for sale to the public shall be subject
to fees as adopted by resolution by the Minidoka County board of county
commissioners. (Ord. 2016-02-01, 2-1-2016)
1-9-3: ONLINE SERVICES:
In order to enhance public accessibility to the county's geographic data, the
county may, but it is not required to, make certain GIS datasets, parcel data
and other information is available on the internet. These online services shall
be subject to fees as adopted by resolution by the Minidoka County board of
county commissioners. (Ord. 2016-02-01, 2-1-2016)
1-9-4: GIS DATA:
   A.   Requests For Data; Costs And Agreement: All requests for GIS data shall
be submitted to Minidoka County and shall be subject to fees as adopted by
resolution by the Minidoka County board of county commissioners. Such requests
are further subject to a "computerized mapping data products license agreement"
(hereinafter referred to as "license agreement") to be executed in each
instance in a form substantially similar to exhibit A attached to the ordinance
codified herein in the office of the Minidoka County clerk. The Minidoka County
assessor is hereby authorized to accept and fulfill such license agreements on
behalf of Minidoka County.
   B.   Exemption From Costs: Persons, organizations or agencies may request to
be exempt from the required fees to acquire Minidoka County's GIS data by
submitting said proposal in writing to the Minidoka County assessor, who shall
forward a recommendation to the board of county commissioners. This may be
approved if the board has determined the following:
      1.   Minidoka County will receive GIS data from the requester, or
services related to the same, that is of comparable or equal value to that
which is to be provided by the county.
      2.   The requester ensures that the data will be protected from improper
or illegal use.
      3.   The benefits to the county and the public outweigh the revenue loss
from the fee waiver. (Ord. 2016-02-01, 2-1-2016)
1-9-5: GIS DATA OWNED BY THIRD PARTIES:
Data stored by the county that is copyrighted by third parties shall not be
conveyed to the public or other agencies without express written permission of
the copyright holder. (Ord. 2016-02-01, 2-1-2016)
1-9-6: USE OF DATA FOR EMERGENCY RESPONSE:
County employees may, without a license agreement or fee, under the direction
of an elected county official or department head, release GIS data to agencies
and personnel engaged in legitimate law enforcement activity or response to
floods, wildfires, acts of terrorism or other emergencies to prevent imminent
peril to life or property. The employee(s) releasing the GIS data shall include
written notification with the released GIS data that its use is limited to
emergency response actions and all other use is strictly prohibited without
appropriate approval in accordance with this chapter. (Ord. 2016-02-01, 2-1-
2016)
1-9-7: PENALTIES:
In addition to any and all remedies available at law or in equity, each
violation of the provisions of this chapter shall be a misdemeanor punishable
as provided in section
1-4-1 of this title. (Ord. 2016-02-01, 2-1-2016; amd. 2016 Code)
TITLE 2
BUSINESS AND LICENSE REGULATIONS
CHAPTER 1
LIQUOR, BEER AND WINE
SECTION:
2-1-1: Title
2-1-2: Authority And Purpose
2-1-3: Licenses Required
2-1-4: Application For License
2-1-5: License Fees
2-1-6: Revocation Of License
2-1-7: Hours Of Sale
2-1-8: Penalties
2-1-1: TITLE:
This ordinance shall be known as the Minidoka County Liquor, Beer, and Wine
Ordinance, and all other ordinances and parts of ordinances and resolutions in
conflict herewith are hereby repealed upon the effective date of this
ordinance. (Ord. 2016-09-13-B, 9-13-2016; amd. 2016 Code; Ord. 2024-08-12, 8-
12-2024)
2-1-2: AUTHORITY AND PURPOSE:
   A.   This ordinance is adopted pursuant to the authority granted to counties
to regulate the sale of liquor, wine, and beer as provided in the Idaho Code,
and the Constitution of the State of Idaho.
   B.   The purpose of this chapter is to establish consolidated rules and
regulations governing the regulation and sale of liquor, wine, and beer. (Ord.
2016-09-13-B, 9-13-2016; amd. Ord. 2024-08-12, 8-12-2024)
2-1-3: LICENSES REQUIRED:
   A.   It shall be unlawful for any person to sell liquor, beer, or wine at
retail or by the drink within the boundaries of Minidoka County without having
first procured a license for the sale of the same from the State of Idaho.
   B.   It shall further be unlawful for any person to sell beer or wine at
retail or by the drink within the boundaries of Minidoka County without having
first procured a County license for the sale of beer or wine. (Ord. 2016-09-13-
B, 9-13-2016; amd. Ord. 2024-08-12, 8-12-2024)
2-1-4: APPLICATION FOR LICENSE:
   A.   Application for license shall be in writing, signed and sworn to by the
applicant upon forms furnished by the County Clerk. Such application shall be
filed by the Clerk and presented to the Board of County Commissioners at the
next regular meeting for approval or rejection, or further consideration.
   B.   All applicants for issuance of a beer license shall be governed by the
provisions of Title 23, Chapter 10 of the Idaho Code in effect as of the date
of this ordinance, or as hereafter amended.
   C.   All applicants for issuance of a wine license shall be governed by the
provisions of Title 23, Chapter 13 of the Idaho Code in effect as of the date
of this ordinance, or as hereafter amended.
   D.   In addition to the statutory requirements of the State of ldaho for
application for a Retail Liquor License issued by the State of ldaho, all
applicants are required to provide the Minidoka County Clerk with a copy of
said license governed by the provisions of Title 23, Chapter 9. Applicants
providing said license will be considered in compliance with the license
documentation requirements of Minidoka County.
   E.   The Board of County Commissioners shall act upon an application for a
retail liquor, beer, or wine license, a transfer, or a renewal thereof within
fourteen (14) days from receipt of said application by the Board of County
Commissioners.
(Ord. 2016-09-13-B, 9-13-2016; amd. Ord. 2024-08-12, 8-12-2024)
2-1-5: LICENSE FEES:
   A.   Pursuant to the provisions of ldaho Code§ 23-916, § 23-1015, § 23-1315,
§ 23-1317, § 23-1005A.
   B.   The license fees shall be collected on a calendar year basis, running
from 1:00 o'clock a.m. July 31st through 12:59 o'clock a.m. of the following
July 30th.
(Ord. 2016-09-13-B, 9-13-2016; amd. Ord. 2024-08-12, 8-12-2024)
2-1-6: REVOCATION OF LICENSE:
The right shall remain at all time vested in the Board of County Commissioners
to revoke or cancel any license for fraud or misrepresentation in its
procurement, for violation of any provisions of this ordinance, for violation
of any state statute regulating the sale and distribution of liquor, wine and
beer, or for conduct or act of the licensee or his employees, or any conduct or
act permitted by him or them on the premises where such business in conducted
tending to render such business or such premises as a public nuisance or menace
to the health, peace, safety or general welfare of the County; provided
further, that revocation or suspension of the state license for sale of liquor,
wine, or beer shall be deemed a prima facie evidence for revocation of
suspension of any license issued by the County as provided herein. (Ord. 2016-
09-13-B, 9-13-2016; amd. Ord. 2024-08-12, 8-12-2024)
2-1-7: HOURS OF SALE:
   A.   No beer or wine shall be sold, offered for sale, or given away upon any
licensed premises between the hour of 1:00 o'clock a.m. until 7:00 o'clock a.m.
   B.   No liquor shall be sold, offered for sale, or given away upon any
licensed premises between the hour of 1:00 o'clock a.m. until 10:00 o'clock
a.m. on Monday, Tuesday, Wednesday, Thursday, Friday, Saturday and Sunday.
   C.   No liquor shall be sold, offered for sale, or given away upon any
licensed premises on Christmas from 1:00 o'clock a.m. to 10:00 o'clock a.m. the
following day. The sale of liquor by the drink, subject to the other
restrictions on hours as set forth in this ordinance, is hereby allowed on
Sundays, Memorial Day and Thanksgiving Day pursuant to the provisions of ldaho
Code Idaho Code § 23-927(1)(2).
   D.   The regulation of hours for sale of liquor as provided in Idaho Code §
23-927 shall apply in addition to the regulations set forth in this ordinance.
(Ord. 2024-08-12, 8-12-2024)
2-1-8: PENALTIES:
Any person violating the provisions of this ordinance shall be punished by a
fine not exceeding Three Hundred and 00/100 Dollars ($300.00), imprisonment in
the county jail for a period not to exceed six (6) months, or by both such fine
and imprisonment. (Ord. 2016-09-13-B, 9-13-2016; amd. 2016 Code; Ord. 2024-08-
12, 8-12-2024)
CHAPTER 2
PAWNBROKERS
SECTION:
2-2-1: Definition
2-2-2: License Required
2-2-3: Application For License; Deposit
2-2-4: Issuance Of License
2-2-5: License Requirements
2-2-6: Investigation By Sheriff
2-2-7: Conditions For Transfer Of License
2-2-8: Posting Of License
2-2-9: Memorandum Of Entry
2-2-10: Receipt For Payment; Pawn Ticket
2-2-11: Record Of Transactions
2-2-12: Reports Available To Law Enforcement
2-2-13: Taking Pawn From Certain Persons Prohibited
2-2-14: Acts Of Employees
2-2-15: Restrictions On Charges
2-2-16: Location Of Business
2-2-17: Revocation Of License
2-2-18: Violation A Misdemeanor
2-2-1: DEFINITION:
Any person within the county who loans money on deposit of personal property or
deals in the selling of the same back again to the pledger or depositor, or who
mortgages security thereon, and takes or receives such personal property into
his possession, is hereby declared to be a "pawnbroker". (Ord. 97-2, 12-8-1997)
2-2-2: LICENSE REQUIRED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to conduct or transact a pawnbroker
business or pawnshop in the county without first having procured a license
therefor as hereinafter provided. (Ord. 97-2, 12-8-1997)
2-2-3: APPLICATION FOR LICENSE; DEPOSIT:
   A.   Information On Application: The application for a pawnbroker's license
shall state the name of the person, and, in case of a firm or corporation, the
names of all the partners in such firm, or of all of the directors, officers
and stockholders of such corporation. The application shall also state the
place, street and number where such business is to be carried out. (Ord. 97-2,
12-8-1997; amd. 2016 Code)
   B.   Deposit: At the time of filing such petition, the applicant shall
deposit fifty dollars ($50.00) for one-fourth (1/4) of a year's fee with the
treasurer of the county for the application to be complete. This sum of money
shall be refunded to the applicant if the license petitioned for is not
granted. If the license is granted, the remaining balance of fees for the year,
one hundred fifty dollars ($150.00), may be paid in full, or the fees may be
paid in quarterly installments. (Ord. 97-2, 12-8-1997)
2-2-4: ISSUANCE OF LICENSE:
No such license shall be issued to any person, corporation, or association
other than the real and actual proprietor of the business and place of business
for which it is issued. (Ord. 97-2, 12-8-1997)
2-2-5: LICENSE REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Contents Of License: The license issued under this chapter shall state
the name of the person to whom issued, the place of business and street number
where such business is located.
   B.   Term: Such license shall entitle the person receiving it to do business
at the place designated in the license for one year from the date of the
license.
   C.   Renewal: The holder of the license may apply to have the license
renewed one month prior to the end of the previous license. (Ord. 97-2, 12-8-
1997)
2-2-6: INVESTIGATION BY SHERIFF:
All applications for a pawnbroker license, or renewal thereof, shall be
presented to the county treasurer. No application shall be acted upon until a
recommendation by the county sheriff to the county treasurer for or against the
application is made. Such recommendation shall be made within thirty (30) days
of the filing of the application. If the sheriff's recommendation is against
granting the license, the sheriff must include reasons for the decision with
the negative recommendation to the county treasurer. The county treasurer shall
not be bound by the sheriff's recommendation. Any adverse finding is appealable
to the county commissioners. (Ord. 97-2, 12-8-1997)
2-2-7: CONDITIONS FOR TRANSFER OF LICENSE:
   A.   Pawnbrokers' licenses are not transferable to any other person, except
by a majority vote of the county commissioners, and the filing of an
application by the person to whom such license is, or may be, transferred or
assigned.
   B.   It shall be unlawful for any person to do business, or attempt to do
business, under a license transferred to him without such approval of the
county commissioners. (Ord. 97-2, 12-8-1997)
2-2-8: POSTING OF LICENSE:
It shall be unlawful for any person to conduct or transact a pawnbroker
business in the county unless he shall keep posted in a conspicuous place in
the place of business the license certificate therefor. (Ord. 97-2, 12-8-1997)
2-2-9: MEMORANDUM OF ENTRY:
Every pawnbroker shall, at the time of each loan, deliver to the person pawning
or pledging any goods, articles or things, a ticket or receipt containing the
substance of the entry required to be made by him in such record book, the
amount of the pledge; and no charge shall be made or received by any pawnbroker
for any such entry, memorandum or note. (Ord. 97-2, 12-8-1997)
2-2-10: RECEIPT FOR PAYMENT; PAWN TICKET:
   A.   Receipt: At the time of the redemption of any pledge, the pawnbroker
shall furnish to the pledger, at his request, a written signed receipt
indicating the exact amount paid to redeem the pledge. The receipt shall be
printed or stamped with the name of the pawnbroker and the address, and shall
be legibly written so that the figures thereon are clearly discernible.
   B.   Pawn Ticket: Every pawnbroker shall prepare and deliver to the pledger
at the time of the pledge a pawn ticket listing the property pledged. (Ord. 97-
2, 12-8-1997)
2-2-11: RECORD OF TRANSACTIONS:
   A.   Information Required: Every pawnbroker shall keep either a record book
or a computer record of transactions. At the time of each loan or receipt of
personal property, an entry shall be made, including the following:
      1.   An accurate account and description of the goods, articles or things
pawned, or received;
      2.   The amount of money loaned or advanced thereon;
      3.   The number of the pawn ticket given to the pledger;
      4.   The time of pawning or receiving such goods, articles or things,
both day and hour; and
      5.   The name, address, social security number, driver's license or
identification number and gender of the person pawning or delivering the goods,
articles or things.
   B.   Deleting Entries: No entry made shall be erased, deleted, obliterated
or defaced.
   C.   Computer Disk Backup: If a computer record is kept, the records must be
copied on a computer disk as a backup record.
   D.   Records Open For Inspection: The book or computer record, as well as
every article or thing pawned, pledged or deposited, shall at all reasonable
times be open to inspection and copying by law enforcement or any officer
directed by the sheriff. (Ord. 97-2, 12-8-1997)
2-2-12: REPORTS AVAILABLE TO LAW ENFORCEMENT:
   A.   Availability Of Records And Tickets: Every pawnbroker or pawnshop
keeper in the county must, if requested, make available to law enforcement
full, true and detailed copies of all pawn tickets and the current pages of the
record book, computer printout or computer disk containing the current records.
These records must set forth an exact description of each article or thing
pawned or received by such pawnbroker or pawnshop keeper during the period
since the last such report. Said tickets and records shall be full, detailed
and correct copies of all entries in the book or computer required to be kept
in section
2-2-11 of this chapter. If no article or thing has been pawned or received, a
report must be made to that effect. Investigative reports from law enforcement
agencies will be available upon request.
   B.   Filing Of Reports; Inspection: Law enforcement shall, upon receipt of
such reports, file them securely in the law enforcement building. The reports
shall be open to inspection only by law enforcement or any officer directed by
law enforcement, or upon any order of the court. (Ord. 97-2, 12-8-1997)
2-2-13: TAKING PAWN FROM CERTAIN PERSONS PROHIBITED:
   A.   Persons Restricted: It shall be unlawful for any pawnbroker, pawnshop
keeper, his servant or employee to receive any goods, articles or things in
pawn or pledge from a person who is obviously either under the influence of
drugs or is mentally challenged, or from a person who is under the age of
eighteen (18) years. (Ord. 97-2, 12-8-1997; amd. 2016 Code)
   B.   Identification: It shall be unlawful to take a pledge from any person
who does not produce a means of identification bearing a photograph of the
person, unless that person is known to the pawnbroker or the person accepting
the pledge. It shall be unlawful for the pawnbroker to accept a pledge from a
person presenting such identification without comparing the identification to
the person presenting it and assuring that the person presenting the
photographic identification is the person pictured thereon. (Ord. 97-2, 12-8-
1997)
2-2-14: ACTS OF EMPLOYEES:
The holder of a pawnbroker's license shall be responsible for any and all acts
of his employees, and for a violation by such employees of the provisions of
this chapter, unless the employee is clearly acting outside the scope of his
employment at the time of such act. (Ord. 97-2, 12-8-1997)
2-2-15: RESTRICTIONS ON CHARGES:
No charges shall be made for restoring stolen property to its rightful owner.
Restitution may be available, however, in cases involving criminal prosecution.
Failure to prosecute shall allow the contract rights to be returned to the
licenser. (Ord. 97-2, 12-8-1997)
2-2-16: LOCATION OF BUSINESS:
No pawnbroker's license shall be issued in any location in which such business
is not permitted by the zoning ordinances of the county or applicable city
ordinance. (Ord. 97-2, 12-8-1997)
2-2-17: REVOCATION OF LICENSE:
The county commissioners may revoke any pawnbroker's license for repeated or
serious violations of the provisions of this chapter. Any licensee shall have
the opportunity for a hearing before such revocation. (Ord. 97-2, 12-8-1997)
2-2-18: VIOLATION A MISDEMEANOR:
Any person, firm or corporation violating any provision of this chapter shall
be guilty of a misdemeanor, and a separate offense shall be deemed committed on
each day during or on which a violation occurs or continues. (Ord. 97-2, 12-8-
1997)
TITLE 3
HEALTH, SANITATION AND ENVIRONMENT
CHAPTER 1
SOLID WASTE DISPOSAL SYSTEM
SECTION:
3-1-1: Purpose
3-1-2: Definitions
3-1-3: Disposal Of Waste At Places Other Than Waste Disposal System Sites
Prohibited
3-1-4: Disposal Only During Regular Hours Of Operation
3-1-5: Prohibited Discharges Or Deposits
3-1-6: Examination Or Testing Required
3-1-7: Method Of Disposal
3-1-8: Transportation Of Solid Waste
3-1-9: User Fee Established
3-1-10: Collection Of Fees
3-1-11: Delinquency Charges
3-1-12: Procedure On Appeal
3-1-13: Hardship Exemption
3-1-14: Unoccupied Building Exemption
3-1-15: Penalties
3-1-1: PURPOSE:
This chapter is established pursuant to Idaho Code Title 31, Chapter 44 to
establish a Solid Waste Disposal System in Minidoka County, Idaho:
   A.   For the purpose of reducing the threat to health posed by uncollected
garbage, refuse, and scrap;
   B.   For the purpose of maintaining the natural and aesthetic setting of the
land, water and air resources of Minidoka County, Idaho;
   C.   For the purpose of promoting the cultural, social, economic, and
sanitary needs of the citizens of Minidoka County as may be necessary from time
to time in establishing a solid waste disposal system;
   D.   In fulfilling the duty of the Board of County Commissioners, pursuant
to Idaho Code Section 31-4403, in maintaining and operating sites and
facilities for the management of solid waste; and
   E.   For providing an adequate means to fund said operations. (Ord. 2016-10-
03, 10-3-2016; amd. Ord. 2021-09-13, 9-13-2021; Ord. 2022-10-17, - - 2022)
3-1-2: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this chapter, the following words and phrases will have the
following meanings unless the context clearly indicates a different meaning:
COMMERCIAL USER: A person who is the owner of a parcel, a building or an
identifiable business or enterprise located on the parcel which is used for
commercial purposes, as determined by the records of the Minidoka County
Assessor, and which is identified by such records in the following
classifications:
   Category 35 - Improvements - Commercial in nature, located on Category 13.
   Category 38 - Improvements - Commercial in nature, located on Category 16.
   Category 40 - Improvements - Commercial in nature, located on Category 18.
   Category 42 - Improvements - Commercial in nature, located on Category 21.
   Category 60 - Improvements on Railroad Rights-of-Way - Improvements located
on railroad rights-of-way under separate ownership.
   Category 61 - Improvements by Lessee Other Than Category 62 - Improvements
made by the tenant or lessee to landlord’s property.
   Category 62 - Improvements on Exempt or Public Land - Taxable improvements
which are owned separately from exempt or public land on which they are
located.
A person shall be considered a separate “commercial user” for each individual
property or building owned or operated by such person. Any of the above
Categories which are directly used in a farming operation shall be excluded
from the definition of “commercial user.”
COUNTY: The County of Minidoka, a political subdivision in the State of Idaho.
HAZARDOUS WASTE: Solid waste which is subject to regulation as hazardous waste
by the Environmental Protection Agency, and as defined in Title 40, Code of
Federal Regulations Section 261.
HEAVY USER: A person who is the owner of a parcel, a building or an
identifiable business or enterprise located on the parcel which is used for
commercial purposes and is used as a hotel, motel, large retail, grocery or
wholesale enterprise as determined by the records of the Minidoka County
Assessor, and which is identified by such records in the following
classifications:
   Category 21 - Improvements - Commercial in nature, located on Category 42.
   Category 35 - Improvements - Commercial in nature, located on Category 13.
   Category 38 - Improvements - Commercial in nature, located on Category 16.
INDUSTRIAL USER: A person who is the owner of a parcel, a building or
identifiable business or enterprise located on the parcel which is used for
industrial purposes (manufacturing, processing, assembling, packaging and
storing) as determined by the records of the Minidoka County Assessor, and
which is identified by such records in the following classifications:
   Category 36 - Improvements - Industrial in nature, located on Category 14.
   Category 39 - Improvements - Industrial in nature, located on Category 17.
   Category 43 - Improvements - Industrial in nature, located on Category 22.
LANDFILL: Any sanitary landfill constructed by the County, dedicated to the
County; or leased, operated or maintained by the County, or in conjunction with
other counties as from time to time designated by the Board of Commissioners.
NON-CONFORMING USER: A person who is the owner of a parcel, a building or
dwelling which has multiple solid waste users as herein defined in this
chapter. When the Minidoka County Assessor, after a physical inspection of the
property, determines different solid waste users occupy the same space, the
Minidoka County Assessor shall determine the appropriate fee (residential,
commercial, exempt, etc.) to be assessed to the owner.
PERSON: Any person, firm, corporation, association, municipality, public
utility, or other such entity, as is recognized by the State of Idaho.
RESIDENTIAL/ DOMESTIC USER: Any person who is the owner of an identifiable
dwelling located on private property, as defined by the records of the Minidoka
County Assessor, which has been identified by such records in the following
residential classifications:
   Category 31 - Improvements - Residential improvements located on category
10.
   Category 34 - Improvements - Residential in nature, located on Category 12.
   Category 37 - Improvements - Residential in nature, located on Category 15.
   Category 41 - Improvements - Residential in nature, located on Category 20.
   Category 46 - Manufactured Housing - Structures transportable in one or more
sections, built on a permanent chassis, for use with or without a permanent
foundation.
   Category 48 - Manufactured Housing - Manufactured housing on which a
statement of intent to declare as real property has been filed.
A person shall be considered a separate “domestic user” for each individual
dwelling on property owned or occupied by such person. Each individual living
unit of multi-family buildings, apartments, duplexes, etc., shall be considered
a separate “domestic user”.
SOLID WASTE: All solid material that is useless, unwanted, discarded, or
otherwise considered as waste by the person in possession of it.
SOLID WASTE DISPOSAL SYSTEM: Lands, sites, facilities, equipment, personnel,
and administration necessary for the disposal of solid waste.
TAX EXEMPT USER: A person who is the owner of a parcel of property as
determined by the records of the Minidoka County Assessor and which is
identified by such records in classification Category 81 - Exempt Properties,
and which has located upon such property an occupied building. For the purpose
of this chapter, an occupied building shall include schools, churches,
government buildings, and other buildings that are in actual use during any
part of the year. A person shall be considered a separate “tax exempt user” for
each individual property or individual building on each property owned by such
person.
UTILITY USER: Any company or corporation operating in the State of Idaho under
the jurisdiction of the Idaho Public Utilities Commission and defined by the
Idaho State Tax Commission as “Operating Property” as determined by the records
of the Minidoka County Assessor and which is identified by such records in
classification Category 67 - Operating Property. One Utility User Unit will be
applied to each parcel of land that has occupied buildings that generate solid
waste as herein defined in this chapter. (Ord. 2016-10-03, 10-3-2016; amd. Ord.
2021-09-13, 9-13-2021; Ord. 2022-10-17, - -2022)
3-1-3: DISPOSAL OF WASTE AT PLACES OTHER THAN WASTE DISPOSAL SYSTEM SITES
PROHIBITED:
It shall be unlawful, except at a Solid Waste Disposal Site for any person to
throw away, dump, or discard within the county any type or nature of solid
waste on any public lands, right-of way of any kind, or private land of
another. In addition to the criminal penalties for violation of this section,
civil damages in an amount of three times the actual damages shall be imposed
on any person committing any such act, to be used to restore the dump site to
its previous condition. Such civil action shall be brought in Minidoka County
and for the benefit of the County for violations occurring within the county,
and any remainder of damages collected after restoration of the site, shall be
used for the maintenance and operation of the Minidoka County Solid Waste
Disposal System and enforcement of this chapter. (Ord. 2016-10-03, 10-3-2016;
amd. Ord. 2021-09-13, 9-13-2021; Ord. 2022-10-17, - -2022)
3-1-4: DISPOSAL ONLY DURING REGULAR HOURS OF OPERATION:
No person shall deposit or discharge any of the following substances into or
upon any landfill, or the premises in any landfill as defined above, at a time
other than the regular hours and days in which such landfill is open to public
dumping. (Ord. 2016-10-03, 10-3-2016; amd. Ord. 2021-09-13, 9-13-2021; Ord.
2022-10-17, - - 2022)
3-1-5: PROHIBITED DISCHARGES OR DEPOSITS:
No person shall deposit or discharge any of the following substances into or
upon any landfill in Minidoka County:
   A.   Asbestos.
   B.   Hazardous waste.
   C.   Flammable or explosive liquids, solids or gases.
   D.   Radioactive materials.
   E.   Vehicle chassis or frames.
   F.   Any other substance or material which, in the opinion of the landfill
operator, is unsuitable for discharge or deposit at the landfill because of
actual or potential threat to the health or safety of the landfill operator or
other persons using or associated with the landfill. (Ord. 2016-10-03, 10-3-
2016; amd. Ord. 2021-09-13, 9-13-2021; Ord. 2022-10-17, - -2022)
3-1-6: EXAMINATION OR TESTING REQUIRED:
It shall be the responsibility of any person discharging or depositing
materials at a landfill to insure that materials deposited therein do not
contain any of the foregoing prohibited substances. The landfill operator may
refuse to accept for disposal or discharge any materials which, in his opinion,
may contain any of the substances set forth in Section 5 until such time as the
person desiring to discharge such materials has demonstrated to the
satisfaction of the operator that said materials do not contain any prohibited
substances. The cost for any necessary examination or testing of materials
shall be at the sole cost and expense of any person desiring to discharge or
deposit said materials at the landfill. (Ord. 2016-10-03, 10-3-2016; amd. Ord.
2021-09-13, 9-13-2021; Ord. 2022-10-17, - - 2022)
3-1-7: METHOD OF DISPOSAL:
Every person discharging materials at a landfill shall do so in a manner as
directed by the landfill operator. Any person depositing materials shall
personally contact the landfill operator to obtain directions for disposal of
such material prior to the discharge or deposit of said material at the
landfill. (Ord. 2016-10-03, 10-3-2016; amd. Ord. 2021-09-13, 9-13-2021)
3-1-8: TRANSPORTATION OF SOLID WASTE:
It shall be unlawful for any person to transport any solid waste in Minidoka
County without said waste being tarped, or otherwise sufficiently covered or
secured to prevent the inadvertent or accidental dumping, spillage, or discard
of such solid waste. (Ord. 2016-10-03, 10-3-2016; amd. Ord. 2021-09-13, 9-13-
2021; Ord. 2022-10-17, - -2022)
3-1-9: USER FEE ESTABLISHED:
To fund a portion of the operations of the Minidoka County Solid Waste Disposal
System, the Board of County Commissioners of Minidoka County, Idaho does
hereby, pursuant to Idaho Code Section 31-4404, establish a user’s fee within
Minidoka County, Idaho, to be charged upon each solid waste user (as defined
above) for use of the Minidoka County Solid Waste Disposal Facilities. Such
fees are as follows:
   A.   One Hundred Five and 00/100 Dollars ($105.00 per year per residential/
domestic user.
   B.   Five Hundred Fifty and 00/100 Dollars ($550.00) per year per commercial
user.
   C.   Five Hundred Fifty and 00/100 Dollars ($550.00) per heavy use user.
   D.   Five Hundred Fifty and 00/100 Dollars ($550.00 per year per industrial
user.
   E.   Five Hundred Fifty and 00/100 Dollars ($550.00) per year per utility
user.
   F.   One Hundred Five and 00/100 Dollars ($105.00) per year per tax exempt
user.
   G.   A schedule for gate fees based on materials and volume actually
delivered to the landfill will be adopted by Resolution as the Board of
Minidoka County    Commissioners.
   H.   No user fee shall be charged on the Occupancy/Supplemental or Missed
Roll. (Ord. 2016-10-03, 10-3-2016; amd. Ord. 2021-09-13, 9-13-2021; Ord. 2022-
10-17, - -2022)
3-1-10: COLLECTION OF FEES:
Annual user fees as provided in Section 9 of this chapter shall be collected in
conjunction with annual property taxes by the Minidoka County Treasurer after
assessment of said fees by the Minidoka County Assessor through identification
of residential/domestic, commercial, heavy user, industrial, utility and tax
exempt users pursuant to this chapter. Collection of the per load and per
volume charges herein referred to shall be the responsibility of the operator
of the Minidoka County Waste Disposal System, and shall be payable by the user
at the time of delivery of the solid waste to the landfill, unless billing
arrangements have been approved. (Ord. 2016-10-03, 10-3-2016; amd. Ord. 2021-
09-13, 9-13-2021; Ord. 2022-10-17, - -2022)
3-1-11: DELINQUENCY CHARGES:
All solid waste user fees shall be due and payable in two (2) equal
installments. The first installment shall be paid on or before December 20, and
the second installment shall be due and payable on or before June 20. Any
installment not paid on or before its due date becomes delinquent and shall be
subjected to a penalty of two percent (2%), and shall be subjected to interest
on the amount of the fee and penalty at the rate of one percent (1%) per month,
calculated from January 1 following the year for which the user fee was
imposed. (Ord. 2016-10-03, 10-3-2016; amd. Ord. 2021-09-13, 9-13-2021; Ord.
2022-10-17, - - 2022)
3-1-12: PROCEDURE ON APPEAL:
   A.   Solid Waste Users may file an appeal of the Users Fee with the Board of
Minidoka County Commissioners. An appeal shall be made in writing on a form
provided by the Clerk of the Board of County Commissioners and must identify
the Solid Waste User, the property which is the subject of the appeal and the
reason for the appeal.
   B.   Within thirty (30) days of the appeal of the user fee, the Board of
County Commissioners shall render a decision on said appeal and shall notify
the applicant in writing of such decision.
   C.   Any decision of the Board of County Commissioners may be appealed to
the District Court under the procedures established by the Idaho Administrative
Procedures Act. (Ord. 2016-10-03, 10-3-2016; amd. Ord. 2021-09-13, 9-13-2021;
Ord. 2022-10-17, - -2022)
3-1-13: HARDSHIP EXEMPTION:
Any person who shall establish that payment of the Solid Waste User Fee,
provided by this chapter, would create an extreme hardship may apply for
exemption from said fee, pursuant to the appeal process herein provided. In the
event that said hardship is demonstrated, the Board of County Commissioners
shall abate such portion of the annual user fee as is necessary to alleviate
the hardship imposed by the fee. (Ord. 2016-10-03, 10-3-2016; amd. Ord. 2021-
09-13, 9-13-2021; Ord. 2022-10-17, - -2022)
3-1-14: UNOCCUPIED BUILDING EXEMPTION:
After a physical inspection of any property with improvements that are subject
to the User Fee, established by this chapter, and the Minidoka County Assessor
finds the improvements are uninhabitable or otherwise do not meet the
requirements of this chapter to be charged the User Fee, the Minidoka County
Assessor may make application to the Board of Minidoka County Commissioners to
cancel the fee and remove the fee from that parcel. (Ord. 2016-10-03, 10-3-
2016; amd. Ord. 2021-09-13, 9-13-2021; Ord. 2022-10-17, - -2022)
3-1-15: PENALTIES:
Any person violating any provision of this chapter shall be fined not less than
One Hundred and 00/100 Dollars ($100.00), not more than Three Hundred Dollars
($300.00) for each offense, and/or incarcerated for up to six (6) months in the
county jail for such offense. A separate offense shall be deemed committed on
each day during which a violation occurs or continues. (Ord. 2016-10-03, 10-3-
2016; amd. Ord. 2021-09-13, 9-13-2021; Ord. 2022-10-17, - -2022)
CHAPTER 2
OPEN BURNING
SECTION:
3-2-1: Definitions
3-2-2: Enforcement
3-2-3: Accumulation Of Garbage And Rubbish
3-2-4: Burning Regulated And Restricted
3-2-5: Penalty
3-2-1: DEFINITIONS:
The following terms, as used in this chapter, are defined as follows:
   GARBAGE: All putrescible wastes except sewage, including, but not limited
to: table refuse, swill, offal, waste products of the preparation, consumption
and storage of foodstuffs, animal wastes, animal products or grass clippings.
   NEIGHBORING RESIDENCE: Any occupied dwelling which is owned by someone other
than the person, or that person's designee, who intends to burn items included
in this chapter.
   NORMALLY ACCEPTABLE YARD WASTE: Includes tree limbs, dry leaves, and other
dry vegetation matter produced on premises, except grass clippings, that are
readily burnable without a great concentration of smoke.
   PERSON: An individual, partnership, corporation, association or any limited
liability entity.
   PREMISES: Any publicly or privately owned lot, plot, parcel, or tract of
real property, including an alley, right of way, road, street or highway.
   RESIDENCE: A dwelling, whether a single unit or a unit in a multiple
dwelling construction.
   RUBBISH: All nonputrescible wastes, including, but not limited to,
discarded, worthless and valueless personal property, sod and stumps, except
for normally acceptable yard waste or compost piles. (Ord. 07-03, 11-19-2007)
3-2-2: ENFORCEMENT:
This chapter may be enforced by any peace officer, law enforcement officer,
sheriff or fire marshal. (Ord. 07-03, 11-19-2007)
3-2-3: ACCUMULATION OF GARBAGE AND RUBBISH:
It shall be unlawful to deposit, collect, store, or accumulate, or permit the
deposit, collection, storage or accumulation, of any garbage and/or rubbish
upon land, lots, premises, alleys, rights of way, or roads in the county,
except for normally acceptable yard waste and/or garbage produced on premises.
(Ord. 07-03, 11-19-2007)
3-2-4: BURNING REGULATED AND RESTRICTED:
   A.   Burning Of Garbage: It shall be unlawful to burn any garbage upon land,
lots, premises, alleys, rights of way, roads, streets or highways in the county
within three hundred feet (300') of a neighboring residence.
   B.   Permitted Burning: Nothing in this chapter shall prohibit or amend
existing laws as to the burning of agricultural fields, normally acceptable
yard waste, weeds, ceremonial fires, or prohibit the use of open fires for the
purposes of preparing food for human consumption.
   C.   Time And Manner Of Burning:
      1.   All burning must be conducted during daylight hours and no open
burning may remain burning after sunset.
      2.   All burning must be conducted under constant observation by a
responsible person. (Ord. 07-03, 11-19-2007)
3-2-5: PENALTY:
Any person who violates any of the provisions of this chapter or fails to
comply with any of the terms of this chapter shall be guilty of a misdemeanor
and subject to penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. (Ord. 07-03, 11-19-2007; amd. 2016 Code)
TITLE 4
PUBLIC SAFETY
CHAPTER 1
DISASTER MANAGEMENT
SECTION:
4-1-1: Purpose
4-1-2: Definitions
4-1-3: Department Of Disaster Management
4-1-4: Disaster Management Coordinator
4-1-5: Alternate Coordinator
4-1-6: Immunity From Liability
4-1-1: PURPOSE:
The Minidoka County department of disaster management is created to administer
the disaster management policy of Minidoka County pursuant to the requirements
of Idaho Code section 46-1009. The purposes of this chapter are to provide the
preparation and carrying out of plans for the protection of persons, property,
and the environment within the county in the event of a disaster and to provide
coordination and accounting of disaster management functions with all other
public agencies and effective private persons, corporations, and organizations.
(Ord. 2016-09-13-C, 9-13-2016)
4-1-2: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this chapter, the following terms shall have the meanings
ascribed to them in this section:
   BOARD OR BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS: The board of Minidoka County commissioners.
   DISASTER: An occurrence or imminent threat of widespread or severe damage,
injury or loss of life or property in Minidoka County resulting from any
natural or manmade cause, including, but not limited to, fire, flood,
earthquake, windstorm, wave action, volcanic activity, explosion, chemical
spill, riot, or hostile military or paramilitary action.
   DISASTER MANAGEMENT: The activities required for preparation, mitigation,
response to and recovery from disasters, to the extent of the responsibility of
Minidoka County as may be provided by law, to prevent, minimize, and repair
injury and damage resulting from a disaster.
   LOCAL DISASTER EMERGENCY: A declaration of a local disaster emergency by the
chairman of the board of commissioners or board of commissioners, as provided
by Idaho Code section 46-1011. (Ord. 2016-09-13-C, 9-13-2016)
4-1-3: DEPARTMENT OF DISASTER MANAGEMENT:
   A.   Department Created: There is hereby created the Minidoka County
department of disaster management, which is hereby designated as the disaster
agency maintained by Minidoka County pursuant to Idaho Code title 46, chapter
10.
   B.   Composition: The department of disaster management shall consist of the
disaster management coordinator as its head, and such other personnel and
volunteers as may be appointed or authorized by the board of commissioners.
(Ord. 2016-09-13-C, 9-13-2016)
4-1-4: DISASTER MANAGEMENT COORDINATOR:
   A.   Appointment: The "disaster management coordinator" (hereafter "the
coordinator") means the administrative head of the Minidoka County department
of disaster management, and shall be appointed by the board of commissioners.
The coordinator shall serve at the will of the board.
   B.   Duties: The coordinator shall, with respect to Minidoka County disaster
management:
      1.   Coordinate, supervise, and direct the effort of the Minidoka County
department of disaster management for the accomplishment of the purposes of
this chapter and as may be directed by the board of commissioners.
      2.   Coordinate and direct, in conjunction with the Minidoka County
sheriff and other county elected officials and agencies, the mitigation,
preparedness, response and recovery of all county agencies during a disaster.
Nothing herein shall be deemed to grant or authorize the coordinator to
exercise any supervisory or command of authority over any deputies or employees
of the county public officials, or equipment, goods or materials of said
offices, which shall at all times remain under the authority of the direction
of the respective public official.
      3.   Represent the Minidoka County department/office of disaster
management in all dealings with public or private agencies pertaining to
disaster management and act as a liaison between Minidoka County and other
government and nongovernment emergency or disaster management and response
agencies.
      4.   Coordinate the preparation and implementation of county plans and
programs for disaster management which are consistent with national and state
plans and programs.
      5.   Provide updating and testing of the county disaster operations plan
and training of county personnel for damage assessment, damage survey and
radiological monitoring.
      6.   Coordinate all requests from local governments for disaster
services.
      7.   With prior approval of the board of commissioners, accept the
services of volunteers for the purposes of disaster management on behalf of
Minidoka County on such terms and conditions as designated by the board. The
coordinator shall have no authority to employ or contract with any person or
entity on behalf of Minidoka County except with the express prior authorization
of the board of commissioners.
      8.   Execute all others duties of coordinator as may otherwise be
designated by the board of commissioners as may be permitted by law 1 .
   C.   Exceptions To Authority: Nothing in this chapter shall be deemed or
construed to:
      1.   Interfere with the course or conduct of labor disputes, except that
those actions otherwise authorized by the state disaster preparedness act or
other laws may be taken when necessary to forestall or mitigate imminent or
existing danger to public health or safety; or
      2.   Interfere with the dissemination of news or comment on public
affairs; or
      3.   Affect or limit the jurisdiction or responsibilities of police
forces, sheriffs or their deputies, firefighting forces, local emergency
medical service (EMS) agencies licensed by the state department of health and
welfare EMS bureau, units of the armed forces of the United States, or of any
personnel thereof, when on active duty; or
      4.   Grant any authority to the coordinator to take, appropriate, or
commandeer any public or private property from its rightful owner or possessor
for the purposes of disaster management; or
      5.   Adopt or consent to adoption of any plans or programs, including
state or federal plans or programs, relating to disaster management without
separate consideration and approval of the board of commissioners. (Ord. 2016-
09-13-C, 9-13-2016)
 
Notes
1 1. IC § 46-1011.
4-1-5: ALTERNATE COORDINATOR:
In the event the coordinator is absent or unable to function in that capacity,
the chairman or designated member of the board of commissioners may serve as or
appoint an alternate coordinator. (Ord. 2016-09-13-C, 9-13-2016)
4-1-6: IMMUNITY FROM LIABILITY:
Authorized personnel engaged in disaster management activities and persons,
agencies, or any other entity providing building or premises designated by
proper authority as disaster shelters shall have immunity from liability for
property damage, bodily injury, or death to the extent provided by state or
federal law. (Ord. 2016-09-13-C, 9-13-2016)
CHAPTER 2
AMBULANCE SERVICE
SECTION:
4-2-1: Title
4-2-2: Definitions
4-2-3: License Required; Supervision; Exceptions
4-2-4: Application For Ambulance License
4-2-5: Investigation And Approval Of Application For Ambulance Or Invalid Or
Wheelchair Coach License
4-2-6: Standards For Ambulance Or Invalid Or Wheelchair Coach License Liability
Insurance
4-2-7: Standards For Ambulance Equipment
4-2-8: Ambulance Specifications
4-2-9: Application For Drivers, Technicians And Driver/Technician License
4-2-10: Standards For Drivers, Technicians And Driver/Technicians License
4-2-11: Operation Standards For Ambulance Or Invalid Or Wheelchair Coach
Service
4-2-12: Required Equipment
4-2-13: Responsibility Of Operator
4-2-14: Replacement Or Addition Of Vehicles
4-2-15: License Fees; Duration Of License
4-2-16: Suspension Or Revocation Of License
4-2-17: Compliance Required
4-2-18: Penalties
4-2-1: TITLE:
This chapter shall be known as the MINIDOKA COUNTY AMBULANCE ORDINANCE. (Ord.
1-75, 1-1975)
4-2-2: DEFINITIONS:
The following terms shall, for the purpose of this chapter, unless otherwise
specified, have the meanings respectively ascribed to them:
   AMBULANCE: Any privately or publicly owned motor vehicle that is
specifically designed or constructed and equipped, and is intended to be used
for and is maintained or operated, for the transportation of wounded, injured
or sick patients, which otherwise complies with the provisions of this chapter.
   AMBULANCE CREW: Defined as, and shall consist of, two (2) persons qualified
as: a) driver/technician, b) two (2) drivers/technicians, or c) driver/
technician and technician.
   AMBULANCE OPERATOR OR AMBULANCE BUSINESS: Anyone engaging in the business of
transporting ill, sick or injured persons, for hire, or who, by advertising
representation, or otherwise, holds himself out as engaging in such business.
   AMBULANCE SERVICE CHARGES: Any charge, fare or other consideration for
ambulance service.
   APPOINTED COMMITTEE: A committee appointed annually by the board of county
commissioners and consisting of at least the following members:
