   A.   A licensed physician who is a resident of the county.
   B.   A representative of an agency performing emergency services. This
representative may be: the chief of the fire or police department in the
largest city in the county, or the chief of the largest district fire
department in the county, or a representative of the county sheriff's office.
   C.   A citizen who is a resident of Minidoka County. This citizen shall
possess current certification in first aid, at least through the advanced level
of the American Red Cross or the equivalent.
   DRIVER/TECHNICIAN: A person qualified and licensed as both a driver and
technician independently:
   A.   Driver: Any person may be licensed by Minidoka County who drives an
ambulance or invalid or wheelchair coach when the same is operated by or for an
ambulance operator while engaged in the ambulance business.
   B.   Driver: Any person may be licensed by Minidoka County as a driver who
possesses the following:
      1.   A valid driver's license from the state of Idaho.
      2.   Evidence of completion of Minidoka County sheriff's emergency driver
course or defensive driving course sponsored by the national safety council.
      3.   An advanced first aid card or its equivalent; provided, a license
may be issued pending completion of the emergency driver course or defensive
driving course described in this definition; provided, further, that the person
will complete the above requirements at the earliest possible date or the
license will be immediately revoked.
   Provided, further, a driver's license shall be valid for a period of ninety
(90) days and will not be renewable, as the person will be expected to advance
himself to the category of driver/technician in order to continue to be
licensed for ambulance work.
   INVALID OR WHEELCHAIR COACH: Any motor vehicle specially designed, equipped
and used for the transportation of invalid persons on a rental basis with
driver furnished and which has no first aid equipment, flashing red lights, or
sirens.
   LICENSE HOLDER: Any person to whom an ambulance operator's license has been
issued under the provisions of this chapter, and which license has not been
revoked.
   OPERATION: The receiving, picking up or embarking within the county of
Minidoka of a sick or injured person for transportation or conveyance for hire
to any point within or without the county of Minidoka.
   PATIENT: An individual who is sick, injured, wounded or otherwise
incapacitated or helpless.
   PERSON: An individual, firm, partnership, association, or corporation,
company, or group of individuals acting together for a common purpose, or
organization of any kind, including any governmental agency other than the
United States.
   TECHNICIAN: Any person who is qualified to render first aid and who has
completed an approved emergency technician- ambulance (EMT-A) training course
and has successfully completed written and practical examinations for registry
as a state of Idaho emergency medical technician-ambulance (EMT-A) and has
satisfactorily completed a course in cardiopulmonary resuscitation (CPR). (Ord.
1-75, 1-1975)
4-2-3: LICENSE REQUIRED; SUPERVISION; EXCEPTIONS:
   A.   Required: It shall be unlawful for any person, either as owner agent or
otherwise, to furnish, operate, conduct, maintain, advertise or otherwise be
engaged in the business of service of the transportation of patients in the
ambulance business or operate an invalid or wheelchair coach business within
the county without first obtaining a license therefor from the county
commission as hereinafter provided.
   B.   Supervision: It shall be unlawful for an ambulance, or invalid or
wheelchair coach, to be operated, and no person shall drive, attend or permit
it to be operated, within the county, unless the ambulance, the invalid or
wheelchair coach, shall be under the immediate supervision and direction of a
person who is holding a current, valid license as a driver, technician, or
driver/technician.
   C.   Exceptions: Provided, however, that no license shall be required for an
ambulance, or the driver, technician or driver/technician of an ambulance
which:
      1.   Is operated by the state of Idaho, county of Minidoka or other
governmental agency.
      2.   Is operated from a location or headquarters outside of, and
transports patients within, Minidoka County who are picked up beyond the limits
of Minidoka County.
      3.   Is operated from a location or headquarters outside the limits of
Minidoka County, and either:
         a.   Picks up patients beyond the limits of Minidoka County to be
transported to locations within Minidoka County; or
         b.   Picks up patients within Minidoka County to be transported to
locations beyond the limits of Minidoka County; or
         c.   In the case of an emergency where no Minidoka County based
ambulance is available, picks up patients within Minidoka County to be
transported to locations within Minidoka County.
Provided, further, that no such ambulance shall be used to pick up patients
within Minidoka County for transportation to locations within Minidoka County,
unless the driver, technician and technician/driver and the ambulance operator
hold current, valid licenses issued pursuant to this chapter, except as noted
in this subsection C. (Ord. 1-75, 1-1975)
4-2-4: APPLICATION FOR AMBULANCE LICENSE:
Application for ambulance licenses shall be made upon forms prepared or
prescribed by the board of county commissioners, and shall contain:
   A.   The name and address of the applicant and the owner of the ambulance or
invalid or wheelchair coach.
   B.   The trade or other fictitious name, if any, under which the applicant
does business and proposes to do business.
   C.   The training and experience of the applicant in the transportation and
care of patients.
   D.   A description of each ambulance, invalid or wheelchair coach, including
the make, model, year of manufacture, motor and chassis number, current state
license number, the length of time the ambulance or invalid or wheelchair coach
has been in use, the mileage thereof; patient compartment dimensions of the
ambulance or invalid or wheelchair coach, cot and stretcher capacity thereof,
list of equipment carried therein, size, design and color scheme of each
vehicle.
   E.   The location and description of the place or places from which it is
intended to operate.
   F.   Such other information as the board of county commissioners shall deem
reasonably necessary. (Ord. 1-75, 1-1975)
4-2-5: INVESTIGATION AND APPROVAL OF APPLICATION FOR AMBULANCE OR INVALID OR
WHEELCHAIR COACH LICENSE:
   A.   Investigation Of Applicant: The board of commissioners shall, within a
reasonable time after receiving an application for an ambulance or invalid or
wheelchair coach license as provided for herein, cause such investigation as it
deems necessary be made of the applicant and his proposed operation.
   B.   Conditions For License Issuance: The board of commissioners shall issue
a license hereunder for a specified ambulance, invalid or wheelchair coach to
be valid for a period of one year, unless earlier suspended, revoked or
terminated, when they find that:
      1.   The appointed committee or the county sheriff has caused the
ambulance or invalid or wheelchair coach licensed hereunder to be inspected and
found such ambulance or invalid or wheelchair coach so licensed to be in proper
condition as prescribes by the applicable provisions of this chapter;
      2.   The appointed committee or the county sheriff has certified that the
ambulance or invalid or wheelchair coach equipment sets the minimal
requirements prescribed by this chapter and by which to comply with all
applicable laws, ordinances and regulations relating to health, sanitation and
safety;
      3.   The applicant is a responsible and proper person to conduct and
operate an ambulance or invalid or wheelchair coach business;
      4.   A sufficient number of duly licensed technicians and/or technician/
drivers are employed in such capacities by the ambulance or invalid or
wheelchair coach operator; and
      5.   All the requirements of this chapter and all other applicable laws
and ordinances have been met.
   C.   Inspection Of Vehicles; Certification:
      1.   Prior to the issuance of any ambulance or invalid or wheelchair
coach license hereunder, the board of commissioners shall cause to be inspected
the vehicles, equipment and premises designated in each application hereunder
to determine compliance with the standards prescribed by this chapter, and no
license shall be issued by the county clerk unless the appointed committee of
the county has certified compliance with the requirements and standards of this
chapter.
      2.   Subsequent to the issuance of any ambulance or invalid or wheelchair
coach license hereunder, the board of commissioners shall cause to be inspected
each licensed ambulance or vehicle and its equipment and premises whenever they
deem such inspection to be necessary. The inspection authorized by this
subsection shall be in addition to any other safety or motor vehicle inspection
required to be made for ambulances or invalid or wheelchair coaches or other
motor vehicles under the law or ordinance of the state or the county.
   D.   Determination Of Need: The board of commissioners shall determine the
need for additional ambulance, invalid or wheelchair coach operators and shall
issue additional licenses only if the existing ambulance, invalid or wheelchair
coach operators fail to meet the needs and requirements of the county. (Ord. 1-
75, 1-1975)
4-2-6: STANDARDS FOR AMBULANCE OR INVALID OR WHEELCHAIR COACH LICENSE LIABILITY
INSURANCE:
   A.   Requirements: Each ambulance, invalid or wheelchair coach shall, at all
times when in use:
      1.   Conform with the standards, requirements and regulations provided
for in this chapter for the transportation of patients;
      2.   Maintain equipment conforming with the minimal standards,
requirements, and regulations provided for herein, which equipment shall be in
proper and good condition;
      3.   Comply with, and be subject to, all laws, ordinances and regulations
now in force or that may hereinafter be enacted relative to health, sanitation
and safety of patients and property, including motor vehicles; and
      4.   Be equipped with such lights, sirens and special marking to
designate it as an ambulance or invalid or wheelchair coach.
   B.   Inspection: Each licensed ambulance, invalid or wheelchair coach, its
equipment and the premises designated in the application and all records
relating to maintenance and operation of such, shall be open to inspection by
the county, its agents and employees during usual hours of operation.
   C.   Insurance Requirements; Nonliability Of County:
      1.   An ambulance operator shall at all times indemnify and save harmless
the county from and for any and all losses, claims, actions or judgments for
damages or injury to persons or property and losses and expenses caused or
incurred by the ambulance operator and its drivers, technicians and driver/
technicians. No ambulance license shall be issued under this chapter, nor shall
a license be valid after issuance, nor shall any ambulance be operated within
the county unless there is at all times in force and effect insurance coverage
issued by an insurance company licensed to do business in the state of Idaho
for each and every ambulance or invalid or wheelchair coach owned and/or
operated by or for the applicant or licensee, providing the following minimum
limits of liability insurance, in which the county shall be named as a named
insured:
         a.   One hundred thousand dollars ($100,000.00) for property damage to
any one person;
         b.   Two hundred thousand dollars ($200,000.00) for property damage to
any one occurrence;
         c.   Two hundred fifty thousand dollars ($250,000.00) for personal
injury to any one person; and
         d.   Five hundred thousand dollars ($500,000.00) for personal injuries
in any other occurrence.
      2.   The limits of insurance provided herein shall not be deemed the
limitation of the applicant's or licensee's covenant to indemnify and save and
hold harmless the county, and if the county becomes liable for an amount in
excess of the insurance limits herein provided, the applicant or licensee
covenants and/or any of its agents upon whom duties may be imposed by this
chapter, agree to indemnify and save and hold harmless the county from any and
all such losses, claims, actions, judgments or expenses for damages or injury
to persons or property. (Ord. 1-75, 1-1975)
4-2-7: STANDARDS FOR AMBULANCE EQUIPMENT:
   A.   Equipment Required: The required equipment in each ambulance shall
include, at all times when the ambulance is in use as such, equipment adequate
for dressing wounds, splinting fractures, controlling hemorrhages, and
providing a workable and usable condition at all times.
   B.   Equipment List: The following is a list of required equipment
representing the minimum standard for each ambulance vehicle:
      1.   Radio Equipment: Each ambulance shall be equipped and maintained at
all times by the operator with a two-way radio operating on a radio frequency
authorized by the federal communications commission. Such radio communications
shall be between such vehicle and the operator's headquarters, and the county
sheriff's office, Rupert police department, and local hospitals as designated
by the medical communication system.
      2.   Safety Equipment:
         2 sets of seat belts.
         2 hardhats.
         2 fire extinguishers (dry chemical type).
         3 road flares (20 minute type).
         2 3-cell flashlights.
         1 hand spotlight.
         1 car mounted spotlight.
         1 auto jack and tire wrench.
         1 tackograph recording device.
      3.   Stretchers:
         1 all level cot, with multiple position backrest, 4 inch all rubber
wheels, multiple standing levels, contour features 2 sets safety belts, locking
bar, and 4 inch foam mattress and pillow.
         1 portable stretcher with safety straps.
      4.   Blankets And Linen:
         5 crash type blankets.
         1 wool or equivalent blanket for each stretcher; adequate linen for 6
complete changes.
         2 plastic covers for patients.
      5.   Oxygen Equipment:
         1 "H" tank of oxygen or equivalent.
         1 "D" tank of oxygen or equivalent.
         1 medical oxygen manifold.
         1 inhalator with regulator and humidifier.
         4 oxygen masks with hose (2 adult and 2 pediatric).
         4 oxygen canulas with hose.
         1 mechanical resuscitator.
         2 resuscitator masks (1 adult and 1 pediatric).
         Mouth to mouth artificial ventilation airways for adults and children.
         Oropharyngeal airways in adult, child and infant sizes (2 each).
         1 hand operated bag-mask ventilation unit with adult, child, and
infant size masks. Valves must operate in cold weather and unit must be capable
of use with oxygen supply.
         1 portable suction apparatus with wide bore tubing and rigid,
pharyngeal suction tip.
         1 portable oxygen equipment with adequate tubing and adequate mask in
adult, child and infant sizes.
         Connecting hose for oxygen supply for bag-mask resuscitator.
      6.   Tools:
         Pry bar.
         Hacksaw.
         1 wrench, 12 inch with adjustable open end.
         1 screwdriver, 12 inch with regular blade.
         1 screwdriver, 12 inch with Phillips type.
         1 hacksaw with 12 wire (carbide) blades.
         1 pliers, 10 inch vise grip.
         1 5-pound hammer with 15 inch handle.
         2 ropes, each 50 feet long and 3/4 inch in diameter.
      7.   First Aid Equipment:
         3 arm splints (pneumatic type).
         4 leg splints (pneumatic type).
         2 arm splints (padded board type).
         4 ice packs.
         1 combination urinal.
         1 bedpan.
         1 package paper towels.
         4 constricting bands.
         1 OB kit (1 pair of scissors and 2 clamps).
         1 bottle of alcohol.
         1 bottle zephiran chloride.
         Ace bandages:
          8 6-inch.
          8 3-inch.
          8 2-inch.
         1 dozen bandages.
         5 triangular type bandages.
         Airways:
          2 large adult.
          2 small adult.
          2 infant adult.
         Spine boards:
          1 short with straps and cervical collar.
          1 long with straps.
          1 lower extremity traction splint with commercial limb support.
         Slings, padded ankle hitch and traction strap.
          1 orthopedic stretcher.
         2 rolls foil 18 inches by 25 feet (sterilized and wrapped).
         5 soft roll self-adhering type bandages 6 inches by 5 yards.
         36 (8 inches by 71/2 inches) combination sterile dressings.
         24 2-inch roller gauze.
         2 rolls (2 inch) adhesive tape.
         3 pairs of scissors.
         2 rolls (1/2 inch) adhesive tape.
         1 bottle distilled water.
         1 bottle normal saline.
         1 poison kit.
         1 package ammonia inhalants.
         2 surgical masks.
         2 dozen patient tags.
         1 restraint belt with cuffs.
         1 restraint belt.
         2 sandbags (2 by 4 by 12 inches).
         2 large sterile burn sheets.
         2 resuscitubes (1 child and 1 adult).
         1 stethoscope.
         1 blood pressure unit.
         2 mouth gags.
         2 universal dressings 10 inches by 36 inches.
      8.   Technician's Bag: A technician's bag which shall contain the
following:
         1 bandage shears.
         2 flashlights (1 regular and 1 pencil type).
         1 small airway (or assorted sizes).
         1 large airway (or assorted sized).
         6 rolls 3 inch bandages.
         2 rolls 1 inch adhesive tape.
         4 arm splints.
         1 mouth gag.
         6 tongue depressors.
         1 infant oxygen face cone.
         2 assorted Ace bandages.
         3 18-inch pieces surgical rubber tubing.
         10 4 by 4-inch gauze pack.
         2 rolls 11/2 inch or 2 inch adhesive tape.
(Ord. 1-75, 1-1975)
4-2-8: AMBULANCE SPECIFICATIONS:
   A.   Vehicles: All new vehicles purchased, whether as a replacement or in
the creation of a new ambulance service, must conform to current
specifications, as set forth below:
      1.   The ambulance vehicle should have space for a driver, technician and
two (2) litter patients. The patients should be so positioned in the vehicle
that at least one can be given life support in transit. There should be a
permanent separation between the driver's compartment and patient compartment.
The vehicle should be able to carry equipment and medical supplies for
safeguarding personnel and patients under hazardous conditions, and for maximum
emergency medical care, both outside the vehicle and in transit. The emergency
vehicle should be designed to provide maximum safety and comfort for the
patient.
      2.   Minimum space between the head of the litter and the bulkhead of the
vehicle should be at least twenty five inches (25"), including a seat for a
technician so positioned that he can provide respiratory care and
resuscitation.
      3.   Minimum space at the foot of the litter should be five inches (5")
to accommodate traction splints and attendant.
      4.   Minimum space between litters should be fifteen inches (15") so that
a technician can move between litters, and kneel to perform external cardiac
compression and other medical functions.
      5.   While a height of sixty inches (60") is preferable throughout the
interior of the emergency vehicle, the minimal height should be at least fifty
four inches (54") from floor to ceiling. This minimal height provides
approximately thirty nine inches (39") from the top of the litter to the
ceiling, and allows the technician enough room to kneel beside the patient and
to use maximal body weight in performing cardiac compression.
   B.   Inspection:
      1.   The appointed committee, prior to the issuance of an ambulance
license or the renewal thereof, shall inspect each ambulance to determine the
adequacy of equipment and certify to the board of commissioners compliance with
the minimal standards for ambulance equipment. The appointed committee shall
take into consideration the current list of minimal equipment for ambulances
adopted by this chapter, or any amendment thereto, and by the American College
Of Surgeons or its duly authorized committee trauma.
      2.   Prior to the issuance of an ambulance license or the renewal
thereof, the county sheriff shall inspect each ambulance, and certify to the
board of commissioners that it is equipped with siren, red lights, and other
emergency vehicle equipment as required by the Idaho motor vehicle code, and
shall have been inspected to determine safe operating condition of each
vehicle, in compliance with state vehicle inspection laws. (Ord. 1-75, 1-1975)
4-2-9: APPLICATION FOR DRIVERS, TECHNICIANS AND DRIVER/TECHNICIAN LICENSE:
Application for drivers', technicians', and driver/technicians' licenses
hereunder shall be made upon forms prepared or prescribed by the board of
commissioners. No person shall drive or serve as a driver, technician, or
driver/technician with an ambulance licensed hereunder without first procuring
the applicable license from the county. Each license application shall contain
at least the following:
   A.   The applicant's full name, current residence and length of time he has
resided in the county.
   B.   The applicant's age, marital status and other physical attributes. The
applicant must be nineteen (19) years of age or over.
   C.   Whether he has ever been convicted of a felony or a misdemeanor, and,
if so, when, where and for what cause.
   D.   The applicant's training and experience in the transportation and care
of patients, whether he has previously been licensed as a driver, chauffeur,
technician or driver/technician, and, if so, when, where and whether his
license has ever been revoked or suspended in any jurisdiction and for what
cause.
   E.   Affidavits of good character from two (2) reputable citizens.
   F.   Fingerprints and photograph to be taken by the county sheriff's
department.
   G.   Such other information as the board of commissioners shall deem
reasonably necessary to make a determination of compliance with this chapter.
(Ord. 1-75, 1-1975)
4-2-10: STANDARDS FOR DRIVERS, TECHNICIANS AND DRIVER/TECHNICIANS LICENSE:
The board of commissioners shall, within a reasonable time after receiving an
application as provided for herein, cause such investigation as he deems
necessary to be made of the applicant for a driver, technician or driver/
technician license hereunder, valid for a period of one year unless earlier
suspended, revoked or terminated, when he finds that:
   A.   The applicant is not addicted to the use of intoxicating liquors or
narcotics and is a morally fit person.
   B.   The applicant is able to speak, read and write the English language.
   C.   The applicant has been found by a duly licensed physician upon
examination attested to on a form provided by the health officer to be of sound
physique, possessing good eyesight, and free of physical defects or disease
which might impair the ability to drive or attend an ambulance.
   D.   The applicant for either technician or driver/technician license has a
currently valid certificate evidencing successful completion of a course of
training equivalent to the emergency medical technician ambulance course, as
approved by the American College Of Surgeons, department of transportation, and
is being used by the state of Idaho department of environmental protection and
health, emergency medical services program for certification of emergency
medical technicians-ambulance.
   E.   No one shall be licensed as a driver or driver/technician unless he
holds a currently valid driver's license from the state of Idaho, plus evidence
of completion of the county sheriff's emergency driver course or defensive
driving course sponsored by the National Safety Council.
   F.   A license of a driver, technician, or driver/technician issued
hereunder shall not be assignable or transferable. (Ord. 1-75, 1-1975)
4-2-11: OPERATION STANDARDS FOR AMBULANCE OR INVALID OR WHEELCHAIR COACH
SERVICE:
No ambulance license shall be issued, renewed or continue in force unless the
ambulance operator shall:
   A.   Have a minimum of one acceptable ambulance or invalid or wheelchair
coach unit based in the county.
   B.   Equip each ambulance or invalid or wheelchair coach to conform with the
minimal standards, requirements, and regulations provided for herein.
   C.   Maintain each ambulance or invalid or wheelchair coach in mechanically
safe, sound and sanitary condition at all times.
   D.   Have at least two (2) ambulance or invalid or wheelchair coach crews
available for prompt response at all times. Each such crew shall consist of two
(2) appropriately licensed personnel.
   E.   Maintain records on forms specified by the board of commissioners, as
follows:
      1.   Monthly call report.
      2.   Detailed individual call report.
      3.   Annual ambulance or invalid or wheelchair coach service report.
      4.   Daily equipment checkoff list.
      5.   Vehicle maintenance log.
      6.   Patient collection - noncollection report.
      7.   Other records and reports as may be required. (Ord. 1-75, 1-1975)
4-2-12: REQUIRED EQUIPMENT:
   A.   Compliance With State And County Laws: No operator's license shall be
issued unless the county sheriff or his designated officer or agent has
determined, upon personal inspection, that the construction and equipment of
each ambulance proposed to be operated is in full compliance with all laws of
the state of Idaho and ordinances and codes of the county.
   B.   List Of Equipment: Upon making application for an ambulance operator's
license or an invalid or wheelchair coach license, the applicant shall submit a
list of equipment to be carried in each vehicle. This list shall be subject to
approval of the county commission at the time that the applicant license is
before the commission for consideration. The list shall be subject to review
and approval annually at the time of the license holder's renewal and shall be
filed with the county recorder. (Ord. 1-75, 1-1975)
4-2-13: RESPONSIBILITY OF OPERATOR:
It is hereby made the duty of the ambulance operator to supervise his
employees, the drivers of the ambulances, the technicians thereon, and the
ambulance, to assure that at all times such vehicles are in condition to meet
the requirements of this chapter, to assure that a competent licensed driver is
operating the same when making calls, and that a licensed technician be present
and accompany such vehicle. Such operator shall not permit any person who is
under the influence of intoxicating liquor or drugs to drive any ambulance or
to accompany the same as a technician. In case the driver/technician violates
any provision of this chapter, the operator may be held responsible and his
license may be revoked for such violations. (Ord. 1-75, 1-1975)
4-2-14: REPLACEMENT OR ADDITION OF VEHICLES:
Whenever a license holder replaces a vehicle, he shall file with the county
commissioners a description of the vehicle to be placed in use with the name of
the manufacturer, engine and serial numbers, and state motor vehicle license
number. Such information shall also be furnished for any vehicle license or
vehicles being added to the operation. Each new vehicle shall be presented for
inspection according to the provisions of this chapter. (Ord. 1-75, 1-1975)
4-2-15: LICENSE FEES; DURATION OF LICENSE:
   A.   License Term: All licenses authorized to be issued hereunder shall bear
the date of issue and shall expire on December 31 next following the date of
issue, unless sooner suspended, terminated or revoked.
   B.   Fees: The following fees shall be charged by the county clerk, which
fee shall accompany the appropriate application:
      1.   Ambulance or invalid or wheelchair coach license, for each vehicle:
Fifty dollars ($50.00).
      2.   Driver, technician and driver/technician licenses: Two dollars
($2.00).
   C.   License Renewal Procedure: Any license issued pursuant to the
provisions of this chapter may be renewed at the expiration thereof by filing a
proper application and paying the fee required for such license; provided, that
the applicant is then qualified to receive a license, and each applicant being
required to conform with all the requirements as upon original licensing. (Ord.
1-75, 1-1975)
4-2-16: SUSPENSION OR REVOCATION OF LICENSE:
   A.   Any licensee who shall:
      1.   Neglect or refuse to comply with the provisions of this chapter, or
with the conditions under which any license shall be issued; or
      2.   Violate any of the provisions of any ordinance of the county; or
      3.   Violate any provisions of the laws of the state of Idaho;
shall be subject to have his license suspended or revoked. The county clerk,
upon order by the board of commissioners, shall give notice of the suspension
or revocation to the holder of any license issued hereunder, which notice shall
set forth specifically the facts supporting the charges or grounds for which
the license was suspended or revoked, and such notice shall be served on the
holder of such license. The notice of suspension or revocation shall designate
the time and place that a hearing will be held before the board of
commissioners. If the commissioners find that the basis of either the
suspension or revocation is substantiated, the license shall be suspended or
revoked. If such license is suspended, the license and all evidence thereof
shall be surrendered by the holder of such license and shall be held by the
county clerk until the end of the period of suspension; and in the event the
license is revoked, the holder shall be ineligible to obtain another license
until granted by the board of commissioners.
   B.   Upon suspension or revocation of an ambulance license hereunder,
operations shall cease with such ambulance. Upon suspension or revocation of a
driver, technician or driver/technician license, such driver, technician or
driver/technician shall cease to drive or attend an ambulance, and no person
shall employ or permit such individual to drive or attend an ambulance. (Ord.
1-75, 1-1975)
4-2-17: COMPLIANCE REQUIRED:
In addition to the provisions of this chapter, all licensees hereunder shall
comply with all applicable laws, ordinances and regulations now in force or
hereinafter enacted governing the operation of motor vehicles upon highways,
streets, alleys and other public ways. (Ord. 1-75, 1-1975)
4-2-18: PENALTIES:
   A.   Penalty Imposed: Any person violating the provisions of this chapter
shall, upon conviction thereof, be subject to penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. (Ord. 1-75, 1-1975; amd. 2016 Code)
   B.   Injunctive Relief: In addition to the criminal remedies provided
herein, the board of county commissioners may, in its discretion, apply to any
court having jurisdiction over the parties and the subject matter for
injunctive relief to prevent and restrain violation of the provisions of this
chapter. (Ord. 1-75, 1-1975)
CHAPTER 3
911 EMERGENCY COMMUNICATIONS SYSTEM
SECTION:
4-3-1: Emergency Communications System
4-3-1: EMERGENCY COMMUNICATIONS SYSTEM:
   A.   Service Area: There is hereby established a service area of the
emergency communications system, which service area shall include all of
Minidoka County.
   B.   Governing Board: The governing board of the emergency communications
system shall be the board of county commissioners.
   C.   Administrator: The administrator of the emergency communications system
shall be the county sheriff.
   D.   Servicing Calls: The agency to service all 911 emergency communications
system calls shall be the county sheriff's office. (Ord. 02-01, 4-22-2002; amd.
2016 Code)
CHAPTER 4
IODINE PRODUCTS SALES
SECTION:
4-4-1: Report Of Sales
4-4-1: REPORT OF SALES:
   A.   Reporting Requirement: There is hereby enacted a reporting requirement
for all retailers of iodine in concentrations of seven percent (7%) or greater
by volume. For purposes of this section, "retailer" shall mean any vendor who
knows or should have known that a sale is to an end user of iodine product.
   B.   Information And Identification Required: A reporting form will be
provided by the county and require disclosure of name, address, telephone
number, vehicle, and at least one form of photo identification.
   C.   Failure To Comply A Misdemeanor: It shall be a misdemeanor for any
retail vendor of iodine in concentrations of seven percent (7%) or greater to
sell iodine without requiring disclosure of the above information, for failure
to gather said information, or for failure to disclose the said information
when requested by law enforcement agents. (Ord. 02-02, 6-24-2002)
CHAPTER 5
GENERAL OFFENSES
SECTION:
4-5-1: Loitering Near Jail
4-5-2: Use Of Firearms Prohibited
4-5-3: Curfew; Firearms Discharge; Loitering In Certain Area
4-5-4: Firearms And Dumping In Certain Area
4-5-5: Penalty
4-5-1: LOITERING NEAR JAIL:
   A.   Prohibited Acts:
      1.   It shall be a misdemeanor for any person to loiter within thirty
feet (30') of the county jail, to talk to, attempt to talk to, or to pass or
attempt to pass any message or communication of any kind or description to any
person in the custody of the county sheriff in the county jail or fenced areas
surrounding the said jail, unless such person shall have the express permission
of the sheriff or one of his deputies for the occasion in question or is
visiting during visiting hours prescribed by the county sheriff.
      2.   It shall be a misdemeanor for any person, whether upon an authorized
visit or not, to deliver, or attempt to deliver any foodstuffs, liquids,
medicines, drugs or other substance or substances of any kind or description to
a person who is confined to the county jail or the fenced areas surrounding the
county jail, or to any person who is a trustee of the county jail, unless such
delivery to the trustee is made pursuant to business of the trustee, authorized
by the county sheriff or unless the matter to be delivered to any other
prisoner is first submitted for inspection to the sheriff or one of his
deputies, and permission for the delivery or attempted delivery is first
expressly given by said sheriff or deputy.
   B.   Prosecution; Lack Of Permission Or Consent: In a trial upon an offense
described in subsection A1 or A2 of this section, the prosecution shall not
have the affirmative burden of showing a lack of permission or consent by the
proper authority, but a lack of such permission or consent shall be presumed
unless the presumption be overcome by evidence offered by either side which
raises a reasonable doubt of the absence of the permission or consent required.
(Ord., 5-24-1971, eff. 7-1-1971; amd. 2016 Code)
4-5-2: USE OF FIREARMS PROHIBITED:
   A.   Emerald Lake:
      1.   No person shall shoot or cause to be shot any pistol, rifle, shotgun
or other firearm or air rifle or pellet gun upon or onto or over the
recreational area maintained by the county in section 11, township 10 south,
range 23, East Boise meridian, commonly known as Emerald Lake.
      2.   Any person in possession of any of the foregoing firearms, air
rifles or pellet guns at Emerald Lake shall be asked to leave the premises by
the designated caretaker at the recreation area or any law enforcement officer
or county commissioner, and if he shall fail to leave the recreation area
immediately after having been so asked to leave, he shall be guilty of a
misdemeanor. (Ord., 12-8-1971, eff. 12-14-1971; amd. 2016 Code)
   B.   Kimama Butte:
      1.   It shall be unlawful for any person to possess or discharge a rifle
and/or a handgun upon the following real property situated in the county, and
known as Kimama Butte:
         Township 8 south, range 22, Minidoka County, state of Idaho.
         Section 5: NE1/4.
      2.   Any violation of this subsection B is declared to be a misdemeanor.
(Ord. 82-8-1, 8-9-1982)
4-5-3: CURFEW; FIREARMS DISCHARGE; LOITERING IN CERTAIN AREA:
   A.   Definitions: The following terms, as used in this section, are defined
as follows:
   FIREARM: Any rifle, pistol, gun, revolver, air gun, BB gun or other device
in which the propelling force is gunpowder, a spring, air or other similar
force.
   LOITER: To remain on the "premises", as defined in this section, or any
property, either public or private, immediately adjacent to said premises after
being requested to leave by any law enforcement officer or private property
owner.
   PREMISES: The real property owned by Minidoka County and adjacent to exit
208 ("parcel no. 1") in Minidoka County and the real property ("parcel no. 2")
located at 410 South 100 East Minidoka County, state of Idaho, more
particularly described as:
      Parcel No. 1:
      A portion of the S1/2NE1/4 of Section 8, Township 10 South, Range 23
East, Boise Meridian, and described as follows:
      Beginning at the NW corner of the SW1/4NE1/4 of said Section 8, Township
10 South, Range 23 East B.M., thence South along the West line of said SW1/
4NE1/4, 1320.0 feet, more or less, to the Southwest corner thereof; thence
East, along the South line of said SW1/4NE1/4, 908.0 feet, more or less, to a
point in the Northwesterly right of way line of Interstate Project No. I-IG-
80N-3(3)206 Highway Survey; thence along said Northwesterly right of way line
as follows: North 76°12' East, approximately 107.0 feet; Thence North 64°51'
East, 573.49 feet; thence North 47°37'30" East, 397.54 feet to a point which
bears North 60°09' West, 50.0 feet from Station 107+94.06 of relocated State
Highway 27 approach to Interchange No. 1 of said Interstate Project No. I-IG-
80N-3(3)206 Highway Survey; thence Northeasterly along the Northwesterly right
of way line of said relocated State Highway 27, 903.0 feet, more or less to the
North line of the SE1/4NE1/4 of said Section 8; thence West along the North
line of the S1/2NE1/4 of said Section 8, 2270.0 feet, more or less to the Place
of Beginning.
      Parcel No. 2:
      Lot 7, less the North 25 feet of the West 1500 feet, in Section 15,
Township 10 South, Range 24 East of the Boise Meridian.
   B.   Enforcement: This section may be enforced by any peace officer or law
enforcement officer of the state of Idaho.
   C.   Use Of Premises:
      1.   The premises shall be closed to the public between one-half (1/2)
hour after sunset and one-half (1/2) hour before sunrise each and every day and
night.
         a.   All persons are required to leave the premises by one-half (1/2)
hour after sunset and shall not enter the premises before one-half (1/2) hour
before sunrise.
         b.   No person shall allow any motor vehicle, boat, tent, camper or
trailer to remain on the premises during the period in which the premises is
closed to the public.
      2.   It shall be unlawful to mark, deface, disfigure, injure, tamper
with, destroy or remove any buildings, tables, benches, signs, notices, posts,
markers, gate, fence or other structures, facilities or equipment whatsoever
erected, constructed, owned or placed therein by the county or other
governmental entity, either real or personal.
   D.   Discharge Of Firearms: It shall be unlawful for any person, not a peace
officer of the state of Idaho acting in his official capacity, to discharge or
cause to be discharged any firearm on the premises, not in necessary self-
defense.
   E.   Loitering: It shall be unlawful for any person to loiter upon the
premises or upon any real property immediately adjacent to the premises. (Ord.
96-3, 9-30-1996; amd. 2016 Code)
4-5-4: FIREARMS AND DUMPING IN CERTAIN AREA:
   A.   Definitions: For the purpose of this section, the following terms shall
have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection:
   FIREARM: Any rifle, pistol, gun, revolver, or other device in which a
projectile is discharged from the device by the use of gunpowder or similar
substance.
   PREMISES: The real property located at 450 North Meridian, Minidoka County,
Idaho, more particularly described as follows:
      Township 8 South, Range 24, East, Boise Meridian, Minidoka County, Idaho.
      Section 32:
      The North One-Half (N1/2) of said Section 32, Less Tracts C, D, and H;
and
      The North One-Half of the South One-Half (N1/2S1/2) of said Section 32,
Less Tracts C, G, and H and Also Less the East One-half of the East One-Half of
the Northeast One-Quarter of the southeast One-quarter (E1/2E1/2NE1/4SE1/4) of
said Section 32.
   B.   Enforcement: This section may be enforced by an authorized peace
officer in the state of Idaho.
   C.   Use Of Premises: The premises may be used for any lawful purpose,
except that it will be unlawful to use the premises for:
      1.   Target practice or concentrated shooting practice or establishment
of a shooting range. Hunting of birds and mammals is specifically allowed in
compliance with all applicable hunting regulations.
      2.   Dumping of any garbage, appliances, dead animals or other refuse.
(Ord. 08-01, 10-20-2008; amd. 2016 Code)
4-5-5: PENALTY:
Any person violating any provision of this chapter shall be subject to penalty
as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. (2016 Code)
CHAPTER 6
ANIMAL CONTROL
SECTION:
4-6-1: License Permitted; Fees
4-6-2: Tag And Collar; Taking Up Dogs
4-6-3: Control Of Dogs
4-6-4: Reclaiming Impounded Dogs; Adoption; Euthanization
4-6-5: Responsibility Of Head Of Household
4-6-6: Interference With Person Seizing Dog
4-6-7: Entering Private Property
4-6-8: Penalty
4-6-1: LICENSE PERMITTED; FEES:
   A.   All fees set under this Chapter shall be set by Resolution of the
county.
   B.   The owner or any person who is keeping or harboring a dog within the
county, may pay to the Minidoka Joint Animal Control Facility for its special
revenue account an annual license fee for each dog so kept or harbored an
amount as established by the board of commissioners. The license fee shall be
paid at the Minidoka Joint Animal Control Facility, who shall issue in return a
receipt designating the name and address of the owner or custodian paying the
license fee, the number of the license tag assigned, the sex of the dog, a
brief description of the dog, and the amount paid for such license.
   C.   A numbered license tag corresponding to the number listed on the
receipt shall be delivered to the license application with a receipt.
   D.   The implant of a chip at the Minidoka Joint Animal Control Facility,
with payment of related fee at that facility, shall waive any licensing fee for
five (5) years.
   E.   The license shall be effective only to the end of the calendar year
which the same is issued. (Ord. 2021-12-20, 12-20-2021)
4-6-2: TAG AND COLLAR; TAKING UP DOGS:
Any peace officer, animal control officer, or other designated person, may
seize and impound any dog,
   A.   At large, off the owner’s property, without an attendant or master, not
securely confined or leashed whether by tether or trained voice command so that
it does not stray; or
   B.   That threatens, aggressively intimidates or harasses, or bites any
person, livestock, poultry, or domestic animal. (Ord. 2021-12-20, 12-20-2021;
amd. Ord. 2023-10-30, 12-10-2023)
4-6-3: CONTROL OF DOGS:
   A.   Dogs which Disturb Neighborhood: No person shall own, keep, or harbor
any dog which by loud, continued or frequent barking, howling, or yelping shall
annoy or disturb any neighborhood or person. A dog shall not be permitted to
urinate or defecate upon the property of any person other than the dog’s owner,
unless it is immediately cleaned. Violation of this section is an infraction
punishable as provided in
4-6-8 .
   B.   Dogs at Large: Any person who permits any dog owned or possessed or
harbored by him to be, or run at large without a competent and responsible
attendant or master, within the County, or willfully or negligently fails,
neglects, or refuses to keep any such dog securely confined within the limits
of his own premises when not under the immediate care and control of a
competent and responsible attendant or master, shall be guilty of an infraction
punishable as provided in
4-6-8 .
   C.   Vicious Dogs:
      1.   Definitions:
         SECURE ENCLOSURE: One from which the vicious dog cannot escape and for
which exit and entry is controlled by the owner or tenant of the premises or
owner of the vicious dog.
         VICIOUS DOG: Any animal which, when not physically provoked,
physically attacks, wounds, bites, aggressively chases, harasses, or otherwise
injures any person, poultry, livestock, or any domestic animal who is not
trespassing.
      2.   It shall be unlawful for the owner of a vicious dog, or for the
owner or tenant of premises on which a vicious dog is present, to harbor a
vicious dog outside a secure enclosure.
      3.   It shall be unlawful for the owner of a vicious dog, or for the
owner or tenant of premises on which a vicious dog is present, to fail to
maintain the enclosure so that the vicious dog cannot escape the enclosure.
      4.   It shall be unlawful for any person to remove a vicious dog from a
secure enclosure unless the dog is restrained in a manner sufficient to control
the dog.
      5.   Penalty and Sentencing: Persons guilty of a violation of any of the
provisions of this subsection
4-6-3 (C), shall be guilty of a misdemeanor subject to penalties of up to one
hundred eighty days in jail, a one thousand dollar fine, up to 2 years of
probation, and restitution for damages. Further, at sentencing on a violation
of this subsection, the court may in its discretion, in the interest of public
safety, order the owner to have the vicious dog destroyed or may direct the
appropriate authorities to destroy the dog. Both the prosecution and the owner
of the dog may present evidence relevant to the propriety of the destruction of
the vicious dog.
      6.   A vicious dog may be seized and impounded during the pendency of
court proceedings pursuant to
4-6-3 (C).
      7.   Nothing in this chapter shall preclude any civil liability as
otherwise provided by law for damages or loss caused by a vicious dog to
livestock, poultry, or other domestic animals.
   D.   Dog Bites: Any dog which has bitten any person shall be surrendered to
a peace officer or animal control officer. The dog shall be inspected by a
licensed veterinarian and quarantined, if necessary, as may be required under
state law. No inspection or quarantine is required if reliable, current medical
records are provided showing evidence of current immunizations for hydrophobia.
If it is determined during the observation period that the dog has hydrophobia,
the dog shall be euthanized by the veterinarian. Payment of the actual costs of
inspection, keeping the dog, examining the dog, monitoring the dog’s condition
during the period of observation, or euthanization will be assessed by fee. If
the dog is not claimed by its owner and/or person responsible for the animal
within the observation period, it shall be destroyed.
   No dog which has bitten a person shall be adopted out or surrendered to a
third party if the owner or other person responsible for the animal is not
located.
   Any dog which appears likely to be suffering from rabies may be destroyed by
a peace officer or animal control officer if such dog cannot be captured
without exposing such officer or other persons to unreasonable risk of injury.
(Ord. 2021-12-20, 12-20-2021; amd. Ord. 2024-10-30, 12-10-2023)
4-6-4: RECLAIMING IMPOUNDED DOGS; ADOPTION; EUTHANIZATION:
All dogs taken up by a peace or animal control officer shall be delivered to
the Minidoka Joint Animal Control Facility. Facility shall not refuse any dog.
Dogs shall not be held at any other location, except those delivered to a
veterinarian as directed by the Facility. No fostering of dogs outside the
Facility is permitted. Any dog not reclaimed, adopted, or otherwise committed
to an entity engaged in the legal rescue, adoption or otherwise providing homes
for dogs, within twenty-one (21) days shall be euthanized.
Any dog may be reclaimed at the Minidoka Joint Animal Control Facility by the
owner or other person entitled upon payment of any related fees as established
by the county by resolution. Fees shall be paid to the Minidoka Joint Animal
Control Facility and a receipt shall be issued. Fees may include bail out,
vaccination, quarantine, boarding, and other related fees as established by
resolution.
An unlicensed dog which will be kept or harbored within the county, upon
release, shall not be released until the person reclaiming such dog as
purchased a current license and any related fees as established by resolution
incurred related to the dog.
After the five (5) day period for dogs taken up as found in Idaho Code 25-2804,
rather than euthanizing the dog, the animal control officer may then take steps
to adopt the dog to a third person. Any third person shall pay all impoundment
and adoption fees against the dog and have the dog properly licensed before the
dog may be surrendered to such third person.
Minidoka Joint Animal Control Facility may waive impoundment, adoption, and
other fees for an entity engaged in the legal rescue, adoption, or otherwise
providing homes for dogs.
Adoption to a third person is available by Minidoka Joint Animal Control
Facility as provided in this section. Adoption fees shall be established by the
county by resolution and include any needed spay or neuter costs. No dog shall
be surrendered to any such third person unless the dog has been spayed or
neutered, if needed, by a licensed veterinarian. This spay and neuter
requirement may be waived for an entity regularly engaged in the legal rescue,
adoption, or otherwise providing homes for dogs. (Ord. 2021-12-20, 12-20-2021)
4-6-5: RESPONSIBILITY OF HEAD OF HOUSEHOLD:
The responsibility for compliance with all provisions of this chapter shall
rest upon the head of the household at which a dog is being kept or harbored
whether the ownership of such dog is claimed by any person residing in said
household. The parents or guardians of minor children with whom said minor
children are residing shall be deemed to be the owners of the dog of a minor
child residing with them for purposes of this section. A husband and wife or
two (2) or more adults living together may be jointly charged as heads of the
household where a dog is kept or harbored if they fail to comply with their
obligations under this chapter. (Ord. 2021-12-20, 12-20-2021)
4-6-6: INTERFERENCE WITH PERSON SEIZING DOG:
It shall be unlawful for any person to hinder or molest any police officer or
animal control officer who is attempting to perform any act authorized under
this chapter. (Ord. 2021-12-20, 12-20-2021)
4-6-7: ENTERING PRIVATE PROPERTY:
In the enforcement of the provisions of this chapter, any peace officer or
animal control officer is authorized to enter upon private property to capture
a dog running at large or to destroy a rabid or vicious dog, but the authority
granted by this section does not authorize entry into any building on private
property without the consent of the person entitled to control of said
building. It shall be the responsibility of the county to repair any damage to
property or clean up any mess created by the actions of a peace officer or
animal control officer in the pursuit or destruction of a dog on private
property. (Ord. 2021-12-20, 12-20-2021)
4-6-8: PENALTY:
Any person who shall violate any of the provisions of this chapter shall be
guilty of an infraction unless otherwise provided, and upon conviction thereof
shall be punished as follows:
   A.   An admission of guilt or entry of judgment to any such violation shall
result in a penalty of not more than fifty dollars ($50.00) for the first such
violation.
   B.   Upon a subsequent admission of guilt or entry of judgment for
violations of the provisions of this chapter, a penalty of not more than one
hundred dollars ($100.00) shall be assessed.
   C.   Upon a third admission of guilt or entry of judgment for violation of
the provisions of this chapter, a penalty of not more than three hundred
dollars ($300.00) shall be assessed for each subsequent violation. Failure to
pay shall constitute a misdemeanor.
   D.   Violations of
6-4-3 (C), Vicious Dogs, is a misdemeanor punishable as outlined in
4-6-3 (C)(5). (Ord. 2021-12-20, 12-20-2021; amd. Ord. 2024-10-30, 12-10-2023)
CHAPTER 7
MASS GATHERINGS
SECTION:
4-7-1: Title
4-7-2: Authority And Purpose
4-7-3: Definitions
4-7-4: Licensing Requirements
4-7-5: Conditions For Issuing License
4-7-6: Application For License
4-7-7: License Issuance
4-7-8: Removal Of Structures
4-7-9: Revocation Of License
4-7-10: Violation; Penalty
4-7-1: TITLE:
This chapter shall be known as the MINIDOKA COUNTY MASS GATHERING ORDINANCE.
(Ord. 2014-04-28, 4-28-2014)
4-7-2: AUTHORITY AND PURPOSE:
   A.   This chapter is adopted pursuant to the authority granted to counties
to regulate mass gatherings as provided in the Idaho Code and the constitution
of the state of Idaho.
   B.   The purpose of this chapter is to establish consolidated rules and
regulations governing mass gatherings. (Ord. 2014-04-28, 4-28-2014)
4-7-3: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this chapter, the following terms shall have the meanings
ascribed to them in this section:
   ASSEMBLY: A company of persons gathered together at any location at any
single time for any purpose.
   PERSON: Any individual natural human being, partnership, corporation, firm,
company, association, society or group. (Ord. 2014-04-28, 4-28-2014)
4-7-4: LICENSING REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   License Required: No person shall permit, maintain, promote, conduct,
advertise, act as entrepreneur, undertake, organize, manage or sell or give
tickets to an actual or reasonably anticipated assembly of three hundred (300)
or more people, whether on public or private property unless a license to hold
the assembly has first been issued by the Minidoka County commissioners, the
application for which must be submitted to the commissioners at least sixty
(60) days in advance of the assembly. A license to hold an assembly issued to
one person shall permit any person to engage in any lawful activity in
connection with the holding of the licensed assembly.
   B.   License And Fee: A separate license shall be required for each location
in which three hundred (300) or more people assemble or can reasonably be
anticipated to assemble; the fee for each license shall be as set by the board
of county commissioners of Minidoka County.
   C.   Ticket Sales: A license shall permit the assembly of only up to the
maximum number of people stated in the license. The licensee shall not sell
tickets to nor permit to assemble at the licensed location more than the
maximum permissible number of people.
   D.   Location Of Event: No license shall be issued to any anticipated
assembly of three hundred (300) or more people where said location may be
hazardous, dangerous or detrimental to the public health, safety and welfare
unless appropriate safety provisions have been met.
   E.   Exceptions:
      1.   This chapter shall not apply to any regular established, permanent
place of worship, stadium, athletic field, arena, auditorium, coliseum, school
or other similar permanently established place of assembly for assemblies which
do not exceed by more than two hundred fifty (250) people the maximum seating
capacity of the structure where the assembly is held.
      2.   This chapter shall not apply to government sponsored fairs held on
regularly established fairgrounds nor to assemblies required to be licensed by
other ordinances and regulations of the county, nor to assemblies within any
incorporated municipality within the county.
      3.   This chapter shall not apply to any place at which auctions and/or
sales are held which do not exceed by more than two hundred fifty (250) people
the maximum capacity of the structure or outdoor location where the assembly of
the participants and/or buyers of items for auction or sale are held. (Ord.
2014-04-28, 4-28-2014)
4-7-5: CONDITIONS FOR ISSUING LICENSE:
   A.   Number Of Persons At Assembly: Before an applicant may be issued a
license, the applicant shall first determine the maximum number of people which
will be assembled or admitted to the location of the assembly; provided, that
the maximum number shall not exceed the maximum number which can reasonably
assemble at the location of the assembly in consideration of the nature of the
assembly; and provided that, where the assembly is to continue overnight, the
maximum number shall not be more than is allowed to sleep within the boundaries
of the location of the assembly by the zoning or health ordinances of the
county.
   B.   Requirements At Applicant's Expense: Before an applicant may be issued
a license, the applicant shall provide proof that the applicant will furnish at
the applicant's own expense before the assembly commences:
      1.   Health Requirements:
         a.   Potable water, meeting all federal and state requirements for
purity, sufficient to provide drinking water for the maximum number of people
to be assembled at the rate of at least one gallon per person per day and water
for bathing at the rate of at least ten (10) gallons per person per day.
         b.   Separate enclosed toilets for males and females, meeting all
state and local specifications, conveniently located throughout the grounds,
sufficient to provide facilities for the maximum number of people to be
assembled at the rate of at least one toilet for every three hundred (300)
females, and at least one toilet for every three hundred (300) males; an
efficient sanitary means of disposing of waste matter deposited therein, which
is in compliance with all state and local laws and regulations.
         c.   A sanitary method of disposing of solid waste, in compliance with
state and local laws and regulations, sufficient to dispose of the solid waste
production of the maximum number of people to be assembled at the rate of at
least two and one-half (21/2) pounds of solid waste per person per day,
together with a plan for holding and a plan for collecting all such waste at
least once each day of the assembly and sufficient trash cans with tightfitting
lids and personnel to perform the task.
         d.   Physician licensed to practice in the state of Idaho, or
qualified emergency medical technician (EMT) or paramedic, sufficient to
provide the average medical care enjoyed by residents of Idaho for the maximum
number of people to be assembled at the rate of at least one physician or EMT
or paramedic for every two thousand five hundred (2,500) people, together with
an enclosed covered structure where treatment may be rendered, and at least one
emergency ambulance available for use at all times.
         e.   The above health requirements heretofore set forth are to be
minimum requirements only. The plans for the health requirements shall be
submitted to the South Central health district for approval at least thirty
(30) days prior to the proposed assembly.
      2.   Lighting: If the assembly is to continue during hours of darkness,
illumination sufficient to light the central area of the assembly, to include
the medical and health facilities, at the rate of at least five (5) foot-
candles, but not to shine unreasonably beyond the boundaries of the enclosed
location of the assembly.
      3.   Parking: A parking area inside of the assembly grounds sufficient to
provide parking space for the maximum number of people to be assembled at the
rate of at least one parking space for every four (4) persons. In the event
that the site and access to it cannot handle the number of people expected to
attend the assembly, the sheriff of Minidoka County may require the promoter to
provide parking at other sites with transportation between the parking site and
the site of the assembly to be provided by the promoter.
      4.   Telephones: Telephones connected to outside lines sufficient to
provide service for the maximum number of people to be assembled, at the rate
of at least one separate line and receiver for each two thousand (2,000)
persons, and to be placed in accessible locations throughout the assembly area.
      5.   Camping Facilities: If the assembly is to continue overnight,
camping facilities shall be provided by the promoter at the site of the
assembly and said facilities shall be in compliance with all federal and state
requirements sufficient to provide camping accommodations for the maximum
number of people to be assembled. In the event that temporary camping
facilities are not available at the site of the proposed assembly, the promoter
shall provide temporary camping facilities elsewhere which shall be approved by
the health department of Minidoka County.
      6.   Security Guards; Bond: Either regularly employed, duly sworn off
duty peace officers of the state of Idaho or other qualified individuals
sufficient to provide adequate security for the maximum number of people to be
assembled at the rate of at least one security guard for every two hundred
fifty (250) people as a minimum shall be provided by the promoter. A list of
the security guards shall be presented to the Minidoka County sheriff for
approval at least thirty (30) days prior to the proposed assembly. In the event
the county sheriff requires extra help to provide security for the proposed
assembly, the promoter shall deposit with the county a cash bond in the amount
of five thousand dollars ($5,000.00) with a higher bond to be required if the
county commissioners determine it to be necessary.
      7.   Fire Protection: Fire protection, including alarms, extinguishing
devices and fire lanes and escapes, sufficient to meet all federal, state and
local standards for the location of the assembly and sufficient emergency
personnel to efficiently operate the required equipment. The plan for fire
protection and emergency personnel shall be presented to the fire district for
approval at least thirty (30) days prior to the proposed assembly.
      8.   Traffic Control: All traffic control shall be approved by the county
sheriff and the appropriate highway district at least thirty (30) days prior to
the proposed assembly. The promoter shall provide an emergency entrance and
exit to and from the site of the proposed assembly and said emergency entrance
and exit shall be kept open at all times for the use of emergency vehicles. The
promoter is responsible for providing traffic control personnel who shall be
approved by the sheriff at least thirty (30) days prior to the proposed
assembly.
      9.   Noise Control: If the assembly is to include the use of
amplification devices, the sound emitting from such devices shall not be
plainly audible within any place of residence not the source of the sound.
Additionally, the sound emitting from such devices must be minimized during the
hours of twelve o'clock (12:00) midnight through seven o'clock (7:00) A.M.
Control and enforcement of noise amplification is the responsibility of the
promoter.
      10.   Insurance Policy:
         a.   An insurance policy, filed with the clerk of the district court,
underwritten by an insurance company licensed to do business in Idaho in the
minimum amount of one million dollars ($1,000,000.00), which shall indemnify
and hold harmless Minidoka County or any of its agents, officers, servants and
employees from any liability or causes of action which might arise by reason of
granting this license, and from any cost incurred in cleaning up any waste
material produced or left by the assembly, at the site or surrounding areas.
         b.   At the discretion of the board of Minidoka County commissioners,
a performance bond may be required to be deposited with the county commission
in the amount of fifteen thousand dollars ($15,000.00) to ensure compliance
with all terms of this chapter. In addition, a cash bond in the amount of two
thousand dollars ($2,000.00) may be required to be deposited with the county to
pay for damage to adjoining or nonadjoining properties within one thousand feet
(1,000') of the site of the proposed assembly. (Ord. 2014-04-28, 4-28-2014)
4-7-6: APPLICATION FOR LICENSE:
   A.   Filing Period: Application for a license to hold an actual or
anticipated assembly of three hundred (300) or more persons shall be made in
writing to the county commissioners at least sixty (60) days in advance of such
assembly.
   B.   Sworn Statement Required: The application shall contain a statement
made upon oath or affirmation that the statements contained therein are true
and correct to the best knowledge of the applicant and shall be signed and
sworn to or affirmed by the individual or "person" (see definition herein)
making application in the case of a corporation, by all partners in the case of
a partnership or by all officers, by all members of such association, society,
or group, or if there are no officers, by all members of such association,
society or group.
   C.   Contents: The application shall contain and disclose:
      1.   The name, age, residence and mailing address of all persons required
to sign the application, and, in the case of a corporation, a certified copy of
the articles of incorporation together with the name, age, residence and
mailing address of each person holding ten percent (10%) or more of the stock
of said corporation.
      2.   The address and legal description of all property upon which the
assembly is to be held, together with the name, residence and mailing address
of the record owner(s) of all such property.
      3.   Proof of ownership of all property upon which the assembly is to be
held or a statement made upon oath or affirmation by the record owner(s) of all
such property that the applicant has permission to use such property for an
assembly of three hundred (300) persons or more.
      4.   The nature or purpose of the assembly.
      5.   The total number of days and/or hours during which the assembly is
to last.
      6.   The maximum number of persons which the applicant shall permit to
assemble at any time, not to exceed the maximum number which can reasonably
assemble at the location of the assembly in consideration of the nature of the
assembly, or the maximum number of persons allowed to sleep within the
boundaries of the location of the assembly by the zoning ordinances of the
county if the assembly is to continue overnight.
      7.   The maximum number of tickets to be sold, if any.
      8.   The plans of the applicant to limit the maximum number of persons
permitted to assemble.
      9.   The plan for supplying potable water, including the source, amount
available, and location of outlets.
      10.   The plans for providing toilet and lavatory facilities including
the source, number and location, type, and the means of disposing of solid
waste deposited.
      11.   The plans for holding, collection, and disposing of solid waste
material.
      12.   The plans to provide for medical facilities including the location
and construction of a medical structure, the names and addresses and hours of
availability of physicians and nurses and provisions for emergency ambulance
service.
      13.   The plans, if any, to illuminate the location of the assembly,
including the source and amount of power and the location of lamps.
      14.   The plans for parking vehicles, including the size and location of
lots, points of highway access and interior roads including routes between
highway access and parking lots.
      15.   The plans for telephone service, including the source, number, and
location of telephones.
      16.   The plans for camping facilities, if any, including facilities
available and their location.
      17.   The plans for the use of any amplification devices and the plan for
noise control during the assembly.
      18.   The plans for security including the number of guards, their names,
addresses, credentials and hours of availability. The plans for fire
protection, including the number, type and location of all protective devices,
including alarms and extinguishers, and the number of emergency fire personnel
available to operate the equipment.
      19.   The plans for food concessions and concessionaires who will be
allowed to operate on the ground, including the names and addresses of all
concessionaires and their license or permit numbers.
   D.   Bond; License Fee: The application shall include the bond required and
the license fee. (Ord. 2014-04-28, 4-28-2014)
4-7-7: LICENSE ISSUANCE:
The application for a license shall be processed and issued after proof of
compliance with this chapter has been submitted to the board of county
commissioners. Proof of compliance with this chapter must be submitted to the
commissioners at least fifteen (15) days prior to the beginning of the
assembly. (Ord. 2014-04-28, 4-28-2014)
4-7-8: REMOVAL OF STRUCTURES:
All structures, installations, excavations and construction shall be removed by
the licensee from the site of the assembly at the termination of the event. In
the event this is not accomplished within ten (10) days after the assembly, the
county is authorized to accomplish the removal and charge the cost of the
removal against the performance bond. (Ord. 2014-04-28, 4-28-2014)
4-7-9: REVOCATION OF LICENSE:
The license may be revoked by the county at any time if the conditions
necessary for the issuing of or contained in the license are not complied with,
or if any condition previously met ceases to be complied with. (Ord. 2014-04-
28, 4-28-2014)
4-7-10: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
   A.   Public Nuisance: The holding of any assembly in violation of any
provisions or conditions contained in this chapter shall give cause to the
county to seek injunctive relief for creation of a public nuisance. Said action
shall be brought in any court of competent jurisdiction.
   B.   Violation; Penalty Imposed: Any person who wilfully, knowingly and
intentionally violates any condition upon which he is granted a license shall
be fined up to one thousand dollars ($1,000.00) per offense. Each violation
shall be considered a separate offense. Additionally, anyone holding a mass
gathering in the county without a mass gathering license may be fined up to one
thousand dollars ($1,000.00) or be imprisoned not to exceed six (6) months, or
by both such fine and imprisonment. The criminal provisions of this subsection
are not enforceable against the licensee in the event injunctive relief under
subsection A of this section is granted.
   C.   Right Of Entry: If the county issues a license to the promoter, the
promoter shall allow entry to enforce provisions of this chapter or license.
(Ord. 2014-04-28, 4-28-2014)
CHAPTER 8
RECREATIONAL ACTIVITIES ON WATERWAYS
SECTION:
4-8-1: Purpose
4-8-2: Waterways Code Of Regulations
4-8-1: PURPOSE:
This chapter, and the waterways code of regulations in section
4-8-2 of this chapter, are designed to regulate and control the activities of
persons involved in recreational pursuits on those portions of the Snake River
adjoining the county, and all other public waterways in the unincorporated
areas of the county, to promote the health, safety, comfort, and convenience,
peace and good order of the county and the inhabitants thereof; to make certain
acts unlawful; and to provide a penalty for violation of those acts. (Ord. 93-
1, 7-12-1993)
4-8-2: WATERWAYS CODE OF REGULATIONS:
   A.   Regulation 1: It shall be unlawful for any person to fish, swim, dive
or ski from, or to sunbathe, sit or otherwise loiter on, any boat launching
ramp/docks located on those portions of the Snake River adjoining the county or
any public waterways in the county, and/or any docks extending from shore
marked for the purpose of boat usage in the county.
   B.   Regulation 2: It shall be unlawful for any person to swim or waterski
within a boat launching area located in the county. Such areas shall include
all water between the "Slow, No Wake" regulatory buoys and the shoreline,
excluding any marked areas where swimming or waterskiing is specifically
permitted.
   C.   Regulation 3: It shall be unlawful for any person to drive a boat
through or within any "No Wake" area at a speed greater than a "No Wake" speed.
"No Wake" areas shall include all water between any "Slow, No Wake" regulatory
buoys and the shoreline.
   D.   Regulation 4: It shall be unlawful for any person to drive a boat in a
manner, direction or speed that is contrary to posted signs or buoys regulating
the manner, direction or speed of boat travel in a specific area.
   E.   Regulation 5: It shall be unlawful for any person to drive a boat
through or within a marked swimming area in the county. It shall also be
unlawful to fish or ski from a marked swimming dock.
   F.   Regulation 6: "No Wake" areas, swimming areas, swimming docks, skiing
docks, fishing docks, boat launching areas, boat launching docks, reduced speed
areas, restricted direction of travel areas, and restricted usage areas shall
be marked and posted, and are hereby established as set forth on the map
attached as exhibit A to the ordinance codified herein, which is incorporated
herein by this reference.
   G.   Regulation 7: It shall be unlawful for any person to pull a waterskier
from or to a dock, or to waterski from a dock unless such dock is designated as
a waterskiing dock. It shall be unlawful for any person to swim, fish, or dive
from, or tie a boat up to, a waterskiing dock. (Ord. 93-1, 7-12-1993)
TITLE 5
PUBLIC WAYS AND PROPERTY
CHAPTER 1
COUNTY ROADS
SECTION:
5-1-1: Irrigation Water On Roadways
5-1-1: IRRIGATION WATER ON ROADWAYS:
   A.   Control Defined: The owner, operator, lessee, tenant and any other
person having dominion or control of the real property from which irrigation
water sprays, sprinkles or otherwise flows shall be presumed to control such
water.
   B.   Water On Roadway Prohibited: Any person having control of irrigation
water who shall cause, suffer, or allow any such water to spray, sprinkle, or
otherwise flow upon the traveled portion of any public highway, road or street
in any manner other than that authorized by law shall be guilty of a
misdemeanor.
   C.   Penalties:
      1.   Every person found guilty of a violation of this section shall be
subject to punishment by a fine in an amount not to exceed three hundred
dollars ($300.00) and imprisonment in the county jail for a period not to
exceed six (6) months, or both such fine and imprisonment.
      2.   Every person, upon conviction for a second or subsequent violation
of this section occurring within one year, shall be punished by a mandatory
minimum fine of three hundred dollars ($300.00) and shall be further subject to
imprisonment in the county jail for a period not to exceed six (6) months, or
both such fine and imprisonment. (Ord. 92-3, 5-22-1992)
TITLE 6
COMPREHENSIVE PLAN AND AREAS OF CITY IMPACT
CHAPTER 1
COUNTY/CITY COMPREHENSIVE PLAN
SECTION:
6-1-1: Plan Adopted
6-1-2: Application Of Plan
6-1-1: PLAN ADOPTED:
The county/city comprehensive plan of May 2001, is adopted in its entirety,
including text, attached maps, and any and all attachments, exhibits,
schedules, and appendices, for any and all implementation and application of
Idaho Code title 67, chapter 65. The said comprehensive plan is intended for
application by the Minidoka County zoning commission in its review of any
applicable recommendations and applications for review, deliberation, and
decision pursuant to the Minidoka County zoning ordinance, and local land use
planning act. (Ord. 01-02, 5-14-2001)
6-1-2: APPLICATION OF PLAN:
The board of county commissioners hereby recognizes and acknowledges that the
said county/city comprehensive plan was formulated and adopted in conjunction
with the city of Rupert, for application in Minidoka County, and the cities of
Rupert, Acequia, and Minidoka, and that there are distinct and differing
comprehensive plans adopted and applied by the cities of Heyburn, Paul, and
North Burley. In recognition of those separate comprehensive plans, and the
acknowledgment by the board of county commissioners of Minidoka County, that
those municipalities have a vested interest in orderly development within the
areas of impact of the respective municipalities, it is the intent of the board
of county commissioners that, to the extent that the county/city comprehensive
plan of May 2001, adopted herein, is inconsistent with the comprehensive plan
of the city of Heyburn, city of Paul, and city of Burley, it is the intent of
the board of county commissioners of Minidoka County to allow the comprehensive
plan of those respective cities to take precedence over the county/city
comprehensive plan adopted herein in the respective areas of impact. To the
extent that they are consistent, the county/city comprehensive plan of May
2001, shall apply in the county and areas of impact. (Ord. 01-02, 5-14-2001)
CHAPTER 2
RESERVED
CHAPTER 3
HEYBURN AREA OF CITY IMPACT
SECTION:
6-3-1: Administration Agreement
6-3-2: Area Of City Impact Description
6-3-3: Map On File
6-3-1: ADMINISTRATION AGREEMENT:
Minidoka County and the city of Heyburn have arrived at an agreement for
administration of the area of impact, which is hereby covenanted, agreed and
stipulated as follows:
   A.   The city's comprehensive plan and any amendments shall apply in the
area of impact.
   B.   The county's zoning ordinance shall be the zoning law of the area of
impact.
   C.   The county's subdivision ordinance shall be the subdivision law of the
area of impact.
   D.   The county's building code regulations shall be the law applicable to
building and related construction activities.
   E.   The parties agree that the fees for the issuance of building permits
within and for the city by the county shall be split with twenty five percent
(25%) going to the city and seventy five percent (75%) going to the county.
Such shall be remitted by the county to the city on a monthly basis. Fees for
building permits for buildings to be built within the Heyburn area of impact
will go one hundred percent (100%) to the county.
   F.   Enforcement of the provisions of ordinances mentioned in the ordinance
codified herein in the city's area of impact vests solely in the county.
   G.   However, the county agrees to give the city notice of all proceedings
affecting real property in the city's area of impact, including: zoning
changes, changes in zoning districts, issuance of special use permits, and
issuance of variances. Notice shall consist of mailing a copy of the same
notice required by law to affected or interested parties defined by Idaho Code
section 67-6509(a) at the same time said notice is sent to said parties. (Ord.
09-03, 4-26-2009)
